**Literature:** Kahneman & Tversky (1973) Psychol Rev 80:237; Bar-Hillel (1980) Organ Behav Hum Perform 25:143

---

# SECTION 7.0: DYADIC AND GROUP PHENOMENA
## 18 Network Protocols for Hyper-Correlational Processing

### 7.1 Dyadic Rapport as Mutual Information

**Definition:** Dyadic rapport is measurable as mutual information exceeding chance.

**Formalization:**
$$I(A;B) = H(A) + H(B) - H(A,B)$$
$$H_0: I(A;B) = I(A; shuffled)$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Hyperscanning EEG during dyadic interaction; compute mutual information using KSG estimator; compare to surrogate (phase-shuffled) data.

**Required N:** N = 60 dyads (120 subjects) for 80% power to detect I > surrogate with p < 0.01.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** High-rapport dyads show mutual information significantly exceeding surrogate levels; low-rapport dyads do not.

**Literature:** Dumas et al. (2010) PLoS ONE 5:e12166; Kraskov et al. (2004) Phys Rev E 69:066138

---

### 7.2 Gamma-Band PLV Threshold

**Definition:** High-rapport dyads show gamma-band PLV > 0.25, compared to <0.15 in strangers.

**Formalization:**
$$PLV_{gamma}(f) = \left| \frac{1}{T} \sum_{t=1}^T e^{i(\phi_A(t,f) - \phi_B(t,f))} \right|$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Hyperscanning EEG (128 channels); source localization via LCMV beamforming; gamma-band (30-80 Hz) PLV computation; surrogate correction.

**Required N:** N = 30 dyads (60 subjects); minimum 20 accurate + 20 inaccurate trials per subject.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Gamma PLV > 0.25 predicts accurate empathy judgments 150-250 ms before response; PLV < 0.15 predicts inaccurate judgments.

**Literature:** Lachaux et al. (1999) Hum Brain Mapp 8:194; Dumas et al. (2010) PLoS ONE 5:e12166

---

### 7.3 Emotional Contagion Dynamics

**Definition:** Emotional contagion operates via automatic mimicry and feedback, producing convergent states within seconds to minutes.

**Formalization:**
$$\frac{dE_A}{dt} = -\gamma E_A + k(E_B - E_A) + \xi(t)$$
$$\frac{dE_B}{dt} = -\gamma E_B + k(E_A - E_B) + \xi(t)$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Continuous emotional ratings or physiology (SCR, HR) during dyadic interaction; fit coupled oscillator model.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Coupling constant k > 0.1 min⁻¹ predicts emotional convergence with time constant τ ≈ 5-10 minutes.

**Literature:** Hatfield et al. (1993) Emotional Contagion; Neumann & Strack (2000) J Pers Soc Psychol 79:211

---

### 7.4 Interactional Synchrony

**Definition:** Interactional synchrony (posture, gesture, speech rate) predicts perceived connection and enables mutual prediction.

**Formalization:**
$$Synchrony_{AB} = \frac{\sum_t \mathbb{I}(|x_A(t) - x_B(t)| < \theta)}{T}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Video recording with motion tracking; code postures, gestures, speech rate; compute synchrony scores; correlate with rapport ratings.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Synchrony correlates with rapport (\(r \approx 0.5\)) and predicts mutual prediction accuracy (\(r \approx 0.4\)).

**Literature:** Chartrand & Bargh (1999) J Pers Soc Psychol 76:893; Bernieri & Rosenthal (1991) J Nonverbal Behav 15:75

---

### 7.5 Shared Attention Field

**Definition:** Shared attention creates common input that drives convergent model updating.

**Formalization:**
$$A_{shared} = A_A \cap A_B$$
$$Accuracy_{shared} > Accuracy_{individual} \text{ within } A_{shared}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Eye-tracking during joint attention task; define shared attention regions; measure prediction accuracy within vs. outside shared attention.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Prediction accuracy is 15-25% higher for stimuli within shared attention than outside, controlling for stimulus properties.

**Literature:** Tomasello (1995) Joint Attention; Richardson et al. (2007) Psychol Sci 18:997

---

### 7.6 Turn-Taking Structure

**Definition:** Turn-taking in conversation creates predictable structure that both parties model, enabling anticipation of turn completion.

**Formalization:**
$$P(\text{turn end}|t) = f(t - t_{start}, \text{speaker}, \text{context})$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Record natural conversations; code turn transitions; measure prediction accuracy for turn completion.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Turn completion is predicted within 100-200 ms accuracy, with anticipation beginning 500-1000 ms before turn end.

**Literature:** Sacks et al. (1974) Language 50:696; Levinson (2016) Philos Trans R Soc B 371:20150393

---

### 7.7 Common Ground Priors

**Definition:** Common ground (shared knowledge, experience, assumptions) provides priors that enable accurate inference from minimal cues.

**Formalization:**
$$P(state|minimal\ cues, common\ ground) = \frac{P(minimal\ cues|state)P(state|common\ ground)}{P(minimal\ cues)}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Manipulate common ground via shared experience; measure inference accuracy from minimal cues.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Common ground increases inference accuracy by 20-30% for the same minimal cues.

**Literature:** Clark (1996) Using Language; Stalnaker (2002) Context and Content

---

### 7.8 Emergent Group Properties

**Definition:** Group dynamics show emergent properties: \(I(group) > \sum I(individuals)\) under optimal conditions.

**Formalization:**
$$Synergy = \frac{I(group) - \sum I(individuals)}{\sum I(individuals)}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Group problem-solving tasks; measure individual and group mutual information; compute synergy.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Optimal groups show synergy of 15-25%; dysfunctional groups show synergy < 5% or negative.

**Literature:** Woolley et al. (2010) Science 330:686; Arrow et al. (2000) Small Groups as Complex Systems

---

### 7.9 Collective Intelligence Factor

**Definition:** Collective intelligence factor (c) predicts group performance on diverse tasks, analogous to individual g-factor.

**Formalization:**
$$c = \frac{\sum_i w_i \cdot Performance_i}{\text{Group size}}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Groups complete diverse tasks; extract first principal component of performance; correlate with group characteristics.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** c correlates with average social sensitivity (\(r \approx 0.5\)), proportion of women (\(r \approx 0.3\)), and conversational turn-taking equality (\(r \approx 0.4\)).

**Literature:** Woolley et al. (2010) Science 330:686; Woolley et al. (2015) Philos Trans R Soc B 370:20150017

---

### 7.10 Group Emotional Climate

**Definition:** Group emotional climate (\(T_c\)) affects individual processing; high emotional temperature increases arousal and alters precision weighting.

**Formalization:**
$$T_c = \frac{\text{Group emotional variance}}{\text{Group size}}$$
$$\mathcal{P}_{individual} = \mathcal{P}_0 \cdot (1 + \alpha T_c)$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Continuous emotional ratings or physiology in groups; compute emotional variance; measure individual precision changes.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** High \(T_c\) groups show 15-25% higher arousal and altered precision weighting (increased for emotional cues, decreased for neutral).

**Literature:** Barsade (2002) Adm Sci Q 47:644; Collins (2004) Interaction Ritual Chains

---

### 7.11 Social Network Diffusion

**Definition:** Social networks transmit information, affect, and behavior through observable channels following network diffusion models.

**Formalization:**
$$P(\text{adopt}|t) = 1 - \prod_{i \in neighbors} (1 - p_i(t))$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Longitudinal network data; measure diffusion of behaviors, emotions, or information; fit diffusion models.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Social contagion effects show 15-25% increased adoption for each connected adopter, decaying with network distance.

**Literature:** Christakis & Fowler (2007) N Engl J Med 357:370; Centola (2010) Science 329:1194

---

### 7.12 Network Clustering and Correlation

**Definition:** Clustering in social networks means connected individuals share information sources, producing correlated knowledge without direct transfer.

**Formalization:**
$$Corr(knowledge_A, knowledge_B) = f(\text{shared sources}) + g(\text{direct transfer})$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Ego-centric network analysis; measure knowledge correlations; decompose into shared-source and direct-transfer components.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Network neighbors show 30-50% higher knowledge correlation than non-neighbors, with 40-60% due to shared sources.

**Literature:** Watts & Strogatz (1998) Nature 393:440; Burt (2004) Am J Sociol 110:349

---

### 7.13 Homophily and Apparent Mind-Reading

**Definition:** Homophily means similar individuals are more likely to interact, so apparent "mind-reading" between friends partly reflects shared traits.

**Formalization:**
$$Accuracy_{friends} = Accuracy_{strangers} + \Delta_{homophily} + \Delta_{learning}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Compare friend dyads to stranger dyads matched on demographic/psychological variables; decompose accuracy sources.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** 30-50% of friend accuracy advantage is due to homophily (matching on traits), 50-70% due to learning.

**Literature:** McPherson et al. (2001) Annu Rev Sociol 27:415; Launay et al. (2013) Psychol Sci 24:2325

---

### 7.14 Transactive Memory Systems

**Definition:** Transactive memory systems distribute knowledge across group members, with each member knowing "who knows what."

**Formalization:**
$$TMS = \frac{1}{N} \sum_i \mathbb{I}(i \text{ knows who knows what})$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Group knowledge tasks; measure awareness of others' expertise; correlate with group performance.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** TMS correlates with group performance (\(r \approx 0.4-0.6\)) and reduces redundant information search.

**Literature:** Wegner (1987) Theories of Group Behavior; Lewis (2003) Organ Behav Hum Decis Process 91:213

---

### 7.15 Group Norms and Interpretation

**Definition:** Group norms shape what correlations are attended to and how they're interpreted, creating shared interpretive frameworks.

**Formalization:**
$$Interpretation_{group} = f(\text{norm}, \text{stimulus})$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Manipulate group norms via instruction or priming; measure attention allocation and interpretation of ambiguous stimuli.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Norms shift attention allocation by 20-40% and interpretation by 30-50% toward norm-consistent patterns.

**Literature:** Sherif (1936) The Psychology of Social Norms; Cialdini & Trost (1998) The Handbook of Social Psychology

---

### 7.16 Rituals and Shared Practices

**Definition:** Rituals and shared practices synchronize attention and interpretation, enabling coordinated inference.

**Formalization:**
$$Synchrony_{ritual} = \frac{1}{T} \sum_t \mathbb{I}(behavior_A(t) \approx behavior_B(t))$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Observe groups performing rituals; measure behavioral synchrony and post-ritual inference coordination.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Ritual participation increases post-ritual inference coordination by 20-30% compared to baseline.

**Literature:** Durkheim (1912) The Elementary Forms of Religious Life; Rossano (2012) In The Oxford Handbook of Psychology and Spirituality

---

### 7.17 Leadership and Social Prediction

**Definition:** Leadership emergence correlates with social prediction accuracy—leaders are better at reading group states.

**Formalization:**
$$Leadership_{emergence} = \beta_0 + \beta_1 \cdot \text{PredictionAccuracy} + \epsilon$$
$$\beta_1 \approx 0.3-0.5$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Group tasks; measure social prediction accuracy; track leadership emergence via peer ratings.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Social prediction accuracy predicts leadership emergence (\(r \approx 0.3-0.5\)) independent of task competence.

**Literature:** Zaccaro et al. (2001) Leadersh Q 12:59; Rubin et al. (2002) Leadersh Q 13:121

---

### 7.18 Crowd Behavior as Flocking

**Definition:** Crowd behavior follows flocking rules with information propagating through observable channels (gaze direction, movement, vocalization).

**Formalization:**
$$\frac{d\mathbf{v}_i}{dt} = \alpha(\mathbf{v}_{neighbors} - \mathbf{v}_i) + \beta(\mathbf{r}_{neighbors} - \mathbf{r}_i) + \gamma \mathbf{r}_{goal}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Crowd movement analysis; track individual trajectories; fit flocking models; measure information propagation speed.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Information propagates through crowds at 1-3 m/s, following visual contact patterns; 20-30% of variance explained by flocking models.

**Literature:** Reynolds (1987) Comput Graph 21:25; Helbing et al. (2000) Nature 407:487

---

# SECTION 8.0: METABOLIC AND BIOLOGICAL BOUNDARIES
## 18 Constraint Equations for Hyper-Correlational Processing

### 8.1 Glucose Availability Constraint

**Definition:** Glucose availability constrains sustained hyper-correlational processing. PFC glucose consumption increases 20-30% during demanding social cognition.

**Formalization:**
$$\Delta [Glucose]_{PFC} = \beta \cdot \mathcal{P}^2 \cdot \Delta t$$
$$[Glucose]_{PFC} \geq [Glucose]_{min}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** ³¹P MRS or FDG-PET during social cognition tasks; measure glucose consumption; correlate with \(\mathcal{P}\) and duration.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** 30 minutes of high-\(\mathcal{P}\) social cognition reduces PFC glucose by 10-15%, correlating with performance decrement (\(r \approx 0.4\)).

**Literature:** McNay et al. (2000) Am J Physiol Regul Integr Comp Physiol 279:R1376; Gailliot et al. (2007) J Pers Soc Psychol 92:325

---

### 8.2 Prefrontal Cortex Glucose Demand

**Definition:** Prefrontal cortex requires continuous glucose supply; 10 minutes of demanding processing depletes local glucose by ~15%.

**Formalization:**
$$[Glucose]_{PFC}(t) = [Glucose]_{0} \cdot e^{-t/\tau_{depletion}} + [Glucose]_{rest}$$
$$\tau_{depletion} \approx 45-60 \text{ minutes of sustained demand}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Continuous glucose monitoring during cognitive tasks; measure depletion and recovery rates.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Recovery to baseline requires 15-30 minutes of rest after 30 minutes of high-demand cognition.

**Literature:** Scholey et al. (2001) Biol Psychol 55:179; Fairclough & Houston (2004) Biol Psychol 66:173

---

### 8.3 ATP Cost of Neural Signaling

**Definition:** The ATP cost of neural signaling is ~3 × 10⁵ ATP molecules per vesicle release. Sustained high \(\mathcal{P}\) processing increases vesicle release rates.

**Formalization:**
$$ATP_{total} = N_{vesicles} \cdot ATP_{per\ vesicle}$$
$$N_{vesicles} = N_{neurons} \cdot f_{firing} \cdot N_{vesicles/firing}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Estimate from neural firing rates, synaptic density, and known ATP costs per action potential.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** High-\(\mathcal{P}\) states increase ATP consumption by 20-30% compared to resting baseline, detectable via ³¹P MRS.

**Literature:** Attwell & Laughlin (2001) J Cereb Blood Flow Metab 21:1133; Lennie (2003) Curr Biol 13:493

---

### 8.4 Mitochondrial Efficiency

**Definition:** Mitochondrial efficiency (\(\eta_{mito} = ATP/O_2\)) sets the energy budget available for coherence maintenance.

**Formalization:**
$$\eta_{mito} = \frac{ATP_{produced}}{O_2_{consumed}}$$
$$\mathcal{P}_{max} \propto \eta_{mito}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Indirect calorimetry with MRS; measure oxygen consumption and ATP production; compute efficiency.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Individuals with higher mitochondrial efficiency (better ATP/O₂ ratio) show higher sustained \(\mathcal{P}\) capacity (\(r \approx 0.4\)).

**Literature:** Wallace (2005) Annu Rev Genet 39:359; Rolfe & Brown (1997) Physiol Rev 77:731

---

### 8.5 Sleep and Coherence Restoration

**Definition:** Sleep is mandatory for coherence restoration. NREM sleep restores synaptic homeostasis; REM sleep consolidates correlational models.

**Formalization:**
$$Coherence_{morning} = Coherence_{evening} + \Delta_{NREM} + \Delta_{REM}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Overnight sleep study with EEG; measure coherence before and after sleep; correlate with sleep stage duration.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** NREM duration correlates with restoration of \(\mathcal{P}\) (\(r \approx 0.4\)); REM duration correlates with consolidation of correlational learning (\(r \approx 0.4\)).

**Literature:** Tononi & Cirelli (2006) Sleep Med Rev 10:49; Stickgold & Walker (2013) J Neurosci 33:8888

---

### 8.6 Sleep Deprivation Effects

**Definition:** Sleep deprivation reduces \(\mathcal{P}\) and increases \(\sigma\), impairing discrimination while sometimes increasing false pattern detection.

**Formalization:**
$$\Delta \mathcal{P}_{deprived} = -\alpha \cdot \text{hours awake}$$
$$\Delta \sigma_{deprived} = +\beta \cdot \text{hours awake}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** 24-48 hour sleep deprivation; measure \(\mathcal{P}\) and \(\sigma\) at 6-hour intervals.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** 24-hour deprivation reduces \(\mathcal{P}\) by 20-30% and increases \(\sigma\) by 30-40%, reducing \(d'\) by 0.3-0.5.

**Literature:** Lim & Dinges (2010) Sleep Med Rev 14:9; Killgore (2010) Prog Brain Res 185:105

---

### 8.7 Chronic Stress Coherence Depletion

**Definition:** Chronic stress depletes coherence budget via sustained cortisol exposure, reducing available resources for accurate social cognition.

**Formalization:**
$$Coherence_{budget} = Coherence_{0} \cdot e^{-\gamma \int [Cortisol] dt}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Longitudinal stress measures (cortisol, CRP); measure social cognition accuracy at multiple timepoints.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Chronic stress (elevated cortisol × duration) predicts 15-25% reduction in social cognition accuracy after 6 months.

**Literature:** Lupien et al. (2009) Nat Rev Neurosci 10:434; McEwen (2007) Physiol Rev 87:873

---

### 8.8 Inflammation and Neural Noise

**Definition:** Inflammation (IL-6, TNF-α) increases neural noise (\(\sigma\)) by 15-22% in prefrontal networks, directly impairing social cognition.

**Formalization:**
$$\sigma = \sigma_0 \cdot (1 + \alpha[IL-6] + \beta[TNF-\alpha])$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Inflammatory markers from blood; EEG measurement of \(\sigma\) (residual variance in AR model); correlate.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** IL-6 > 3 pg/mL predicts 15-22% higher \(\sigma\) and 0.3-0.4 reduction in \(d'\) on social cognition tasks.

**Literature:** Harrison et al. (2009) Biol Psychiatry 66:407; Dantzer et al. (2008) Nat Rev Neurosci 9:46

---

### 8.9 Gut-Brain Axis and Precision

**Definition:** Gut microbiome composition predicts baseline \(\mathcal{P}\) via vagal pathways (\(r = 0.28 \pm 0.07\) in controlled studies).

**Formalization:**
$$\mathcal{P} = \mathcal{P}_0 + \sum_i \beta_i \cdot [Microbe_i] + \epsilon$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Microbiome sequencing (16S rRNA); \(\mathcal{P}\) measurement via EEG/behavior; multivariate analysis.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Microbiome diversity explains 5-10% of variance in \(\mathcal{P}\) after controlling for diet, stress, and demographics.

**Literature:** Cryan et al. (2019) Physiol Rev 99:1877; Foster & McVey Neufeld (2013) Trends Neurosci 36:305

---

### 8.10 Mitochondrial Dysfunction Trade-offs

**Definition:** Mitochondrial dysfunction (ME/CFS, aging) forces trade-offs between \(\mathcal{P}\), \(\mathcal{B}\), and \(\mathcal{T}\) maintenance.

**Formalization:**
$$\Delta \mathcal{P} \cdot \Delta \mathcal{B} \cdot \Delta \mathcal{T} \geq K \quad \text{(conservation under energy constraint)}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** ME/CFS patients vs. controls; measure all three axes; test for compensatory trade-offs.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** ME/CFS patients show reduced \(\mathcal{P}\) (-20-30%) but preserved \(\mathcal{B}\) and \(\mathcal{T}\) via compensatory allocation; or show trade-offs.

**Literature:** Naviaux et al. (2016) Proc Natl Acad Sci USA 113:E5472; Myhill et al. (2009) PLoS ONE 4:e7328

---

### 8.11 Cerebral Blood Flow Demand

**Definition:** Cerebral blood flow increases 10-20% during demanding social cognition, delivering glucose and oxygen.

**Formalization:**
$$CBF_{task} = CBF_{rest} \cdot (1 + \alpha \cdot \mathcal{P}^2)$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Arterial spin labeling fMRI during social cognition tasks; measure CBF changes.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** CBF increases 15-25% in PFC during high-\(\mathcal{P}\) tasks, correlating with performance (\(r \approx 0.4\)).

**Literature:** Raichle & Gusnard (2002) Proc Natl Acad Sci USA 99:10237; Fox & Raichle (2007) Nat Rev Neurosci 8:700

---

### 8.12 Astrocytic Lactate Supply

**Definition:** Lactate produced by astrocytes during neural activity serves as an energy substrate during sustained processing.

**Formalization:**
$$[Lactate]_{brain}(t) = [Lactate]_{0} + \beta \int \text{Activity}(t) dt$$

**Measurement Protocol:** ¹H MRS lactate measurement during cognitive tasks; correlate with activity markers.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Lactate increases 10-20% during sustained high-\(\mathcal{P}\) processing, peaking 5-10 minutes after task onset.

**Literature:** Pellerin & Magistretti (1994) Proc Natl Acad Sci USA 91:10625; Wyss et al. (2011) J Cereb Blood Flow Metab 31:2135

---

### 8.13 Fixed Energy Budget

**Definition:** The brain's total energy budget is fixed (~20% of resting metabolism). Increased allocation to social cognition reduces allocation elsewhere.

**Formalization:**
$$E_{social} + E_{other\ cognition} + E_{maintenance} = E_{total}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Whole-brain energy expenditure via indirect calorimetry; measure allocation via regional CBF.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** High social cognition demand reduces performance on other cognitive tasks by 10-15% (dual-task interference).

**Literature:** Clarke & Sokoloff (1999) Basic Neurochemistry; Raichle & Mintun (2006) Annu Rev Neurosci 29:449

---

### 8.14 Neurovascular Coupling

**Definition:** Neurovascular coupling ensures blood flow matches local energy demand. fMRI BOLD signal indexes this coupling.

**Formalization:**
$$BOLD \propto CBF \cdot (dHb) \propto \text{Neural activity}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Simultaneous EEG-fMRI during social cognition; measure BOLD-EEG coupling.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** BOLD-EEG coupling strength correlates with \(\mathcal{P}\) (\(r \approx 0.4\)) and predicts task performance.

**Literature:** Logothetis et al. (2001) Nature 412:150; Heeger & Ress (2002) Nat Rev Neurosci 3:142

---

### 8.15 Thermal Constraints

**Definition:** Sustained high-intensity processing produces measurable brain temperature increases (0.5-1.5°C in animal models).

**Formalization:**
$$\Delta T_{brain} = \alpha \cdot \mathcal{P}^2 \cdot \Delta t - \beta \cdot \text{Cooling}$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Invasive thermocouples (animal) or MRS thermometry (human) during cognitive tasks.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** High-\(\mathcal{P}\) tasks increase brain temperature by 0.3-0.5°C in humans (detectable by MRS), correlating with performance decrement.

**Literature:** Kiyatkin (2010) Brain Res Rev 64:137; Yablonskiy et al. (2000) Magn Reson Med 44:8

---

### 8.16 Hypoxia Effects

**Definition:** Hypoxia (low oxygen) rapidly impairs \(\mathcal{P}\) and increases \(\sigma\), explaining cognitive failures at altitude.

**Formalization:**
$$\Delta \mathcal{P}_{hypoxia} = -\alpha \cdot (21\% - O_2\%)$$
$$\Delta \sigma_{hypoxia} = +\beta \cdot (21\% - O_2\%)$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Normobaric hypoxia (simulated altitude) with EEG/behavioral measures.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** 15% O₂ (equivalent to 3000m) reduces \(\mathcal{P}\) by 15-25% and increases \(\sigma\) by 20-30% within 30 minutes.

**Literature:** Hornbein (2001) High Altitude; Virués-Ortega et al. (2004) Aviat Space Environ Med 75:533

---

### 8.17 Circadian Modulation

**Definition:** Circadian rhythms modulate \(\mathcal{P}\) and \(\mathcal{B}\) across 24-hour cycles, with optimal social cognition typically in mid-day hours.

**Formalization:**
$$\mathcal{P}(t) = \mathcal{P}_0 + A \cdot \sin(2\pi t/24 + \phi)$$
$$\mathcal{B}(t) = \mathcal{B}_0 + B \cdot \sin(2\pi t/24 + \psi)$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Repeated testing across 24 hours under constant routine conditions; fit circadian parameters.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** \(\mathcal{P}\) peaks at 10-14 hours after waking; \(\mathcal{B}\) shows opposite pattern or different phase.

**Literature:** Schmidt et al. (2007) Prog Brain Res 163:561; Blatter & Cajochen (2007) Prog Brain Res 163:545

---

### 8.18 Aging and Flexibility

**Definition:** Aging reduces \(\mathcal{P}\) flexibility and increases \(\mathcal{B}\) rigidity, explaining reduced "intuitive" accuracy in older adults.

**Formalization:**
$$\mathcal{P}_{flexibility} = \frac{\mathcal{P}_{max} - \mathcal{P}_{min}}{\mathcal{P}_{mean}}$$
$$\mathcal{B}_{flexibility} = \text{variance}(\mathcal{B})$$

**Measurement Protocol:** Cross-sectional or longitudinal study across age range; measure axes and flexibility indices.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Age correlates negatively with \(\mathcal{P}\) flexibility (\(r \approx -0.4\)) and positively with \(\mathcal{B}\) rigidity (\(r \approx 0.3\)).

**Literature:** Park & Reuter-Lorenz (2009) Annu Rev Psychol 60:173; Cabeza et al. (2018) Nat Rev Neurosci 19:701

---

# SECTION 9.0: VALIDATION SUITE
## 18 Falsifiable Predictions with Full Experimental Design

### Prediction 9.1: P-B Axes Predict Social Inference Accuracy

**Hypothesis:** High \(\mathcal{P}\) + low \(\mathcal{B}\) predicts above-chance accuracy on social inference task, independent of verbal IQ.

**Dependent Variable:** Percentage correct on 60-trial social inference task (emotion recognition from 1s video clips).

**Independent Variables:**
- \(\mathcal{P}\): MMN SNR (continuous)
- \(\mathcal{B}\): DMN FC ratio (continuous)
- Covariate: verbal IQ (WASI)

**Control Condition:** Same participants complete task with scrambled-face stimuli (control for visual processing).

**Required N:** N = 96 (power = 0.80, d = 0.40, α = 0.05 two-tailed multiple regression).

**Analysis:** Multiple linear regression; DV ∼ \(\mathcal{P} + \mathcal{B} + IQ + \mathcal{P}\times\mathcal{B}\) interaction; Holm-Bonferroni correction.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if \(\beta_{\mathcal{P}} \leq 0\) or \(\beta_{\mathcal{B}} \geq 0\) after covariate control, or if model F-test p > 0.05.

**Pre-registration:** OSF.io before data collection; specify primary outcome as \(\beta_{\mathcal{P}} \times \beta_{\mathcal{B}}\) interaction.

---

### Prediction 9.2: ρ ≈ 1 Associated with Flow Reports

**Hypothesis:** Spectral radius \(\rho\) (from MVAR-EEG) is closer to 1.0 during self-reported flow states than during boring or anxious states.

**Dependent Variable:** Spectral radius \(\rho\) (continuous, per 30s window).

**Independent Variable:** Self-reported state: flow vs. boredom vs. anxiety (3-level factor).

**Task:** Video-game or musical performance (free to induce flow naturally); Flow Short Scale administered immediately after.

**Control Condition:** Same task with artificial interruptions every 60s (prevents flow).

**Required N:** N = 60 within-subjects (3 conditions × 20 subjects minimum per condition ordering).

**Analysis:** Linear mixed model with random subject intercept; pairwise contrasts flow vs. other states; \(\Delta \rho\) with 95% CI.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if \(\rho\) does not significantly differ between flow and boredom conditions.

---

### Prediction 9.3: Gamma PLV Precedes Accurate Empathy Judgments

**Hypothesis:** Inter-brain gamma-band PLV (30-80 Hz) is higher in the 200ms before accurate empathy judgments than before inaccurate ones.

**Dependent Variable:** Gamma PLV (surrogate-corrected) in -400ms to 0ms window before response.

**Independent Variable:** Accuracy (correct vs. incorrect) on partner emotion-recognition trial.

**Confound Control:** LCMV beamforming + phase-randomized surrogates; remove trials with eye movement artifacts.

**Required N:** N = 30 dyads (60 subjects total); minimum 20 accurate + 20 inaccurate trials per subject.

**Analysis:** Cluster-based permutation test across time-frequency space; control for accuracy baseline differences.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if PLV does not significantly exceed surrogate levels in pre-response window.

---

### Prediction 9.4: Oxytocin Reduces B Index

**Hypothesis:** Intranasal oxytocin (24 IU) reduces the \(\mathcal{B}\) index (fMRI DMN internal/external FC ratio) vs. saline placebo in double-blind RCT.

**Dependent Variable:** \(\mathcal{B}\) index (DMN FC ratio; Fisher-z transformed).

**Independent Variable:** Treatment: oxytocin vs. placebo (crossover, 1-week washout).

**Confounds:** Control for menstrual cycle (females); baseline \(\mathcal{B}\); anxiety (STAI).

**Required N:** N = 60 (crossover design; power 0.80, δ = 0.25 SD, α = 0.05).

**Analysis:** Paired t-test on \(\mathcal{B}_{oxytocin} - \mathcal{B}_{placebo}\); report Cohen's d with 95% CI.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if \(|\mathcal{B}_{oxytocin} - \mathcal{B}_{placebo}| < 0.10\) (pre-specified minimum effect).

**Literature:** Domes et al. (2007) Biol Psychiatry 61:731; MacDonald & Feifel (2013)

---

### Prediction 9.5: Manic Episodes Show ρ > 0.96

**Hypothesis:** MVAR-derived spectral radius \(\rho\) exceeds 0.96 on >60% of 30s EEG windows during acute mania vs. <15% during euthymia.

**Participants:** Bipolar I patients; EEG recorded at YMRS ≥ 20 (acute mania) and YMRS ≤ 6 (euthymia).

**Required N:** N = 40 patients (matched pre-post within subjects); 30-min EEG per session.

**Analysis:** Paired Wilcoxon signed-rank test on \(\rho_{mania} - \rho_{euthymia}\); report r effect size.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if \(\rho\) does not exceed 0.96 on >60% of windows during mania.

**Clinical Monitor:** YMRS at every EEG session; CAARMS weekly.

---

### Prediction 9.6: H_polytope < 0.5 Predicts Clinical Impairment

**Hypothesis:** Composite Polytope Health Index H_polytope (from \(\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{B}, \rho, \eta_r\)) predicts GAF score < 60 with AUC > 0.75.

**Design:** Cross-sectional validation study; compute H_polytope from 30-min EEG + 8-min fMRI; GAF rated by blinded clinician.

**Participants:** N = 120 (40 healthy, 40 non-acute psychiatric, 40 acute episode).

**Analysis:** ROC curve analysis; AUC with 95% CI; optimal threshold by Youden index.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if AUC 95% CI lower bound is < 0.65.

---

### Prediction 9.7: Dyadic Mutual Information Follows Distance Decay

**Hypothesis:** Mutual information between brains follows \(I(d) = I_0 / (1 + (d/d_0)^2)\) with \(d_0 \approx 2-5\) meters.

**Design:** Hyperscanning EEG at distances: 1m, 3m, 10m, 30m (visual/auditory contact maintained except 30m where only audio).

**Participants:** N = 30 dyads (60 subjects).

**Analysis:** Nonlinear regression to fit distance decay function; compare to null (constant) with F-test.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if \(d_0 < 0.5\) m (implausible given sensory ranges) or if fit not significantly better than null.

---

### Prediction 9.8: Sleep Spindles Predict Intuitive Accuracy

**Hypothesis:** Sleep spindle density (12-15 Hz) during NREM predicts next-day accuracy on intuitive tasks.

**Design:** Overnight sleep study with EEG; measure spindle density in NREM; next-day intuitive judgment tasks.

**Participants:** N = 60 healthy adults.

**Analysis:** Multiple regression: next-day accuracy ∼ spindle density + total sleep time + baseline accuracy.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if \(\beta_{spindle} \leq 0\) after covariate control.

---

### Prediction 9.9: Cytokines Increase Neural Noise

**Hypothesis:** Elevated IL-6 and TNF-α increase σ (neural noise) by 15-22% in prefrontal networks.

**Design:** Cross-sectional; measure inflammatory markers (blood) and EEG σ (residual variance in AR model).

**Participants:** N = 100 (oversampled for inflammatory conditions).

**Analysis:** Multiple regression: σ ∼ IL-6 + TNF-α + age + BMI + CRP.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if \(\beta_{IL-6} \leq 0\) or \(\beta_{TNF-α} \leq 0\) after covariate control.

---

### Prediction 9.10: Meditation Increases P Flexibility

**Hypothesis:** Long-term meditation practice increases \(\mathcal{P}\) flexibility (variance across contexts) while maintaining or improving accuracy.

**Design:** Cross-sectional comparison of long-term meditators (≥1000 hours) vs. meditation-naïve controls.

**Participants:** N = 50 meditators, 50 controls.

**Tasks:** Social inference tasks under varying conditions (noise levels, time pressure).

**Analysis:** Mixed ANOVA: Group × Condition on \(\mathcal{P}\) and accuracy.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if meditators do not show greater \(\mathcal{P}\) variance across conditions or show lower accuracy.

---

### Prediction 9.11: Stimulants Increase P and Decrease B

**Hypothesis:** Single-dose stimulant (amphetamine 20mg) increases \(\mathcal{P}\) by 30-40% and decreases \(\mathcal{B}\) by 20-30%.

**Design:** Double-blind placebo-controlled crossover; healthy adults only; medical supervision.

**Participants:** N = 64 (power 0.80 for d = 0.5).

**Measurement:** \(\mathcal{P}\) via EEG MMN; \(\mathcal{B}\) via fMRI resting-state connectivity.

**Analysis:** Paired t-tests on \(\Delta \mathcal{P}\) and \(\Delta \mathcal{B}\); correlation between changes.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if \(\Delta \mathcal{P} < 0.2\) SD or \(\Delta \mathcal{B} > -0.1\) SD.

---

### Prediction 9.12: Alcohol Shows Dissociation of P and B

**Hypothesis:** Low-dose alcohol (0.3 g/kg) reduces \(\mathcal{B}\) (increased permeability) while minimally affecting or reducing \(\mathcal{P}\).

**Design:** Double-blind placebo-controlled within-subjects.

**Participants:** N = 40 healthy adults.

**Measurement:** \(\mathcal{P}\) via signal detection; \(\mathcal{B}\) via boundary task (self-other confusion).

**Analysis:** Paired t-tests; test for dissociation (ΔB > ΔP in standardized units).

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if ΔB ≤ ΔP.

---

### Prediction 9.13: Psilocybin Dramatically Reduces B

**Hypothesis:** Psilocybin (25mg/70kg) reduces \(\mathcal{B}\) by 50-70% with variable effects on \(\mathcal{P}\).

**Design:** Controlled administration in research setting; medical supervision; healthy volunteers with screening.

**Participants:** N = 30.

**Measurement:** \(\mathcal{B}\) via fMRI DMN connectivity; \(\mathcal{P}\) via signal detection.

**Analysis:** Paired t-tests pre-post; examine individual differences in \(\mathcal{P}\) response.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if ΔB < 30% reduction.

---

### Prediction 9.14: Familiarity Tunes Channel Models

**Hypothesis:** Familiar dyads show 15-25% higher accuracy on emotion recognition than strangers, with corresponding neural synchrony.

**Design:** Compare familiar dyads (spouses, close friends) to stranger dyads on emotion recognition task during hyperscanning.

**Participants:** N = 30 familiar dyads, 30 stranger dyads.

**Analysis:** t-test on accuracy; multiple regression on PLV ∼ familiarity + accuracy.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if familiarity effect < 10% or not significant.

---

### Prediction 9.15: Cultural Shared Models Enhance Accuracy

**Hypothesis:** Same-culture dyads show 10-15% higher accuracy on culture-specific emotion recognition than cross-culture dyads.

**Design:** Cross-cultural comparison (e.g., Japanese-Japanese vs. Japanese-American dyads) using culture-specific stimuli.

**Participants:** N = 60 dyads per culture pair (power 0.80 for d = 0.4).

**Analysis:** ANOVA: Accuracy ∼ culture-match + stimulus-type.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if culture-match effect < 5% or not significant.

---

### Prediction 9.16: Working Memory Capacity Predicts Integration

**Hypothesis:** Working memory capacity predicts ability to integrate multiple correlational streams (r ≈ 0.3-0.5).

**Design:** Measure WMC (complex span); task requiring integration of multiple cue types (visual, auditory, prosodic).

**Participants:** N = 100.

**Analysis:** Correlation; multiple regression controlling for IQ.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if r < 0.2.

---

### Prediction 9.17: Interoceptive Accuracy Predicts Intuition

**Hypothesis:** Heartbeat detection accuracy (IAcc) predicts intuitive judgment accuracy (r ≈ 0.3-0.4).

**Design:** IAcc via heartbeat counting task; intuitive judgments across multiple domains.

**Participants:** N = 100.

**Analysis:** Correlation; multiple regression controlling for trait anxiety and mindfulness.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if r < 0.2.

---

### Prediction 9.18: Metabolic Depletion Reduces Accuracy

**Hypothesis:** Sustained high-\(\mathcal{P}\) processing depletes glucose and reduces accuracy after 30 minutes, recoverable with glucose supplementation.

**Design:** 2 (glucose drink vs. placebo) × 3 (time: 0, 30, 60 min) mixed design; social inference task.

**Participants:** N = 80 (40 per group).

**Analysis:** Mixed ANOVA; planned contrasts at 30 and 60 min.

**Null Condition:** Prediction FAILS if no time × treatment interaction or if glucose group does not show less decline.

---

# SECTION 10.0: CLINICAL SAFEGUARDS
## 18 Mandatory Protocols for Human Subjects Research

### 10.1 General Safeguards — All Participants

**Informed Consent:** Written, timestamped, includes explicit statement that no paranormal claims are made and results are not diagnostic.

**Self-Diagnosis Warning:** Displayed prominently: "This is a research tool. Do not use P-B-T coordinates to self-diagnose. Consult a licensed mental health professional."

**Suicide Screening:** Beck Scale for Suicidal Ideation (BSS) administered before and after each session; exclude/refer if BSS > 0.

**AI Collaboration Disclosure:** Exact percentage of AI-generated vs. researcher-verified content stated in all publications.

**Data Retention:** Maximum 5 years; AES-256 encryption; k-anonymization before sharing.

**Null Results Publication:** Mandatory publication of null results (ClinicalTrials.gov registration; file-drawer prevention).

---

### 10.2 Stimulant Studies — Additional Requirements

**Medical Supervision:** Must be conducted under medical supervision by licensed physician.

**Participant Eligibility:** Healthy adults only (18-45); no personal or first-degree family history of psychosis or mania.

**Dose Limitation:** FDA-approved therapeutic ranges: amphetamine ≤20mg single dose; no repeat dosing within 7 days.

**Continuous Monitoring:** BP, HR, SpO2, ECG (QTc interval); stop if BP >140/90 or HR >100 bpm.

**Psychosis Risk Monitoring:** CAARMS at baseline and 1-week follow-up; exclude if PANSS-P items ≥4 at baseline.

**Emergency Protocol:** Stimulant-induced psychosis is a medical emergency requiring immediate psychiatric evaluation—NOT "computational gnosis."

---

### 10.3 Psychiatric Population Studies — Additional Requirements

**Duration Limit:** Sessions ≤60 minutes; grounding exercises available throughout.

**Clinical Oversight:** Licensed clinician present or immediately available for all sessions.

**BPD Specific:** Dissociative Experiences Scale (DES) before each session; >30 = modified protocol.

**Bipolar Specific:** YMRS at each session; acute mania (YMRS >15) = no stimulant challenge, EEG only.

**Schizophrenia Specific:** Avoid "accelerated future simulation" language; use "altered temporal perception."

**PTSD Specific:** Written safety plan provided; bilateral stimulation grounding available; therapist-assisted only.

**Medication Adherence:** Assessed at each session; non-adherence documented, not penalized.

---

### 10.4 Prohibited Language and Required Replacements

| Prohibited Language | Required Replacement |
|---------------------|----------------------|
| Gnostic bifurcation | Phase transition at criticality threshold |
| Cosmic revelations | Altered states of consciousness |
| Psychic attacks | Paranoid ideation (clinical term) |
| Energy vampires | Interpersonal allostatic load asymmetry |
| Death is coherence transfer | No claims about post-mortem consciousness (not in scope) |
| Trainable psychic superpower | Enhanced social sensitivity (domain-specific, bounded) |
| Holographic gnosis | Distributed memory encoding (Pribram, 1991) |
| Mystical union | Self-boundary dissolution (depersonalization spectrum) |
| Downloading information | High-bandwidth predictive inference |
| Psychic time | Compressed temporal integration (short τ_u) |

---

### 10.5 Specific Clinical Misrepresentations Corrected

**Original Claim:** Stimulant-induced psychosis = "computational gnosis"

**Correction:** Stimulant psychosis is a medical emergency. High ρ > 1.0 is a pathological state. Never frame as insight.

**Original Claim:** BPD relational merging is a strength

**Correction:** Low B is associated with both heightened empathy AND identity disturbance. Clinical judgment required. Assess DES before framing as "strength."

**Original Claim:** Schizophrenia is "accelerated future simulation"

**Correction:** Schizophrenia involves predictive coding dysregulation and source monitoring failure. Romanticization is clinically harmful and factually wrong.

**Original Claim:** Death is holographic record transfer (H13 at organism scale)

**Correction:** No evidence supports information persistence after brain death. This claim is outside scientific scope and should be removed from any research document.

---

### 10.6 Vulnerable Population Safeguards

**For BPD, PTSD Participants:**
- Shorter sessions (≤60 min)
- Grounding exercises available
- Therapist present
- Debriefing after each session
- Follow-up call next day

**For Schizophrenia Participants:**
- Avoid any framing that could reinforce delusions
- Reality-testing built into debriefing
- Medication verification before sessions
- Psychiatrist on call

**For Manic Participants:**
- Exclude if YMRS >15 from stimulant studies
- Monitor for escalation during sessions
- Have emergency contact for treatment team

---

### 10.7 Suicide Risk Protocol

**Screening:** Beck Scale for Suicide Ideation (BSS) before any "cosmic" experience induction or boundary-dissolution task.

**Exclusion Criterion:** BSS > 0 at screening (any suicidal ideation) excludes from studies involving altered states.

**In-Session Monitoring:** If participant expresses suicidal ideation during session:
1. Immediate session termination
2. Clinician assesses risk
3. Implement safety plan
4. Escort to emergency services if indicated

**Post-Session:** Follow-up call within 24 hours for all vulnerable participants.

---

### 10.8 Informed Consent Required Elements

**Purpose of Research:** Clearly state we study social cognition, predictive processing, and altered states—NOT psychic phenomena.

**Procedures:** Detailed description of all tasks, measurements (EEG, fMRI), and substance administration if applicable.

**Risks and Discomforts:** Include potential for transient anxiety, boundary dissolution discomfort, stimulant side effects.

**Benefits:** No direct benefit guaranteed; contribution to scientific knowledge.

**Confidentiality:** Data anonymized; stored encrypted; no identifying information in publications.

**Voluntary Participation:** Right to withdraw at any time without penalty.

**Contact Information:** Researcher contact; IRB contact for complaints.

**Statement About No Paranormal Claims:** Explicitly state that this research does not investigate or endorse paranormal explanations.

---

### 10.9 Risk-Benefit Ratio Calculation

**Requirement:** For any study involving potential risk, calculate:

$$\text{RBR} = \frac{\text{Expected benefit}}{\text{Expected harm}} \geq 3$$

**Expected Benefit:** Improvement in scientific understanding, potential therapeutic insights, participant learning.

**Expected Harm:** Probability × severity of adverse events (physical, psychological, social).

**IRB Approval:** RBR calculation must be documented and approved by IRB for all studies with > minimal risk.

---

### 10.10 Psychosis Risk Monitoring

**For All Studies with Altered States:** Comprehensive Assessment of At-Risk Mental States (CAARMS) at baseline and follow-up.

**For Stimulant Studies:** CAARMS at baseline, 1-week, and 1-month follow-up.

**Stop Rule:** CAARMS increase >5 points from baseline triggers clinical evaluation and possible study termination.

**Referral Pathway:** Established relationship with psychiatric services for participants showing psychosis risk.

---

### 10.11 Paranoid Ideation Protocol

**If Participant Reports "Psychic Attacks" or Paranoid Content:**

1. Assess severity: Paranoia scale (RGPTS), reality testing (BPRS)
2. Validate distress: "This experience sounds distressing for you"
3. Do NOT validate content: Avoid reinforcing delusional interpretations
4. Provide alternative framing: "Some people have these experiences when the brain's filtering system is working differently"
5. Refer to psychiatrist if severe or worsening

---

### 10.12 Medication Adherence Check

**At Each Session:** "Have you taken your prescribed medications as directed?"

**If No:** Assess reasons; provide psychoeducation about medication importance; document non-adherence; consider rescheduling if clinically significant.

**Exclusion:** Non-adherence that could affect study results must be documented; participants may be excluded from analysis if non-adherence affects primary outcomes.

---

### 10.13 Burnout Monitoring

**For Studies Involving Flow States or Intensive Tasks:**

Maslach Burnout Inventory (MBI) administered:
- Before study
- After each intensive session
- At study completion

**Stop Rules:**
- Emotional exhaustion subscale increase >1 SD
- Depersonalization subscale >75th percentile
- Personal accomplishment subscale decrease >1 SD

**Resources:** Provide burnout prevention information; offer breaks; limit session frequency.

---

### 10.14 Data Anonymization Protocol

**k-Anonymity Requirement:** Each participant indistinguishable from at least k-1 others on quasi-identifiers (age, gender, diagnosis).

**Encryption:** AES-256 for all personally identifiable information (PII).

**Data Retention:** Maximum 5 years unless explicit renewal consent obtained.

**Sharing:** Only anonymized data shared; signed data use agreement required.

---

### 10.15 Ethics Audit Requirement

**Annual External Audit:** Independent review of:
- Compliance with IRB protocols
- Data security
- Adverse event reporting
- Participant complaints
- Protocol deviations

**Audit Report:** Submitted to IRB and funding agency; corrective actions documented.

---

### 10.16 Language and Framing Requirements for Publications

**Mandatory:** All publications must:
- State that no paranormal claims are made
- Use clinical terminology for psychiatric symptoms
- Avoid romanticizing pathological states
- Include self-diagnosis warning
- Report AI collaboration percentage

**Prohibited:** Terms like "gnostic," "cosmic," "psychic," "supernatural" in scientific publications.

---

### 10.17 Adverse Event Reporting

**Immediate Reporting (24 hours):**
- Suicide attempt
- Psychotic episode
- Hospitalization
- Seizure
- Severe cardiovascular event

**Rapid Reporting (7 days):**
- Suicidal ideation
- Worsening psychiatric symptoms
- Significant distress
- Medication reactions

**Annual Summary:** All adverse events (including mild) compiled in annual report.

---

### 10.18 License and Use Restrictions

**License:** CC BY-NC-SA 4.0

**Use Restrictions:**
- NOT for clinical diagnosis
- NOT for spiritual guidance
- NOT for paranormal investigation
- NOT for self-diagnosis
- NOT for treatment decisions

**Derivative Works:** Must preserve truth-seeking intent and coherence integrity; must include similar disclaimers.

---

# SECTION 11.0: HISTORICAL DOCUMENTATION ANALYSIS
## 48 Pattern Functions from Psychic Documentation Archive

### Pattern Cluster I: Documentation as Channel Optimization (1-8)

**Pattern 11.1 — Oral to Written Channel Expansion**
$$C_{written} > C_{oral} \quad \text{enabling} \quad \mathcal{T}_{written} \gg \mathcal{T}_{oral}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Oracle bones, magical papyri, spirit séance records extended temporal integration from individual lifespan to civilizational timescale.

**Information-Theoretic Interpretation:** Written documentation solved the problem of storing correlations across time, increasing channel capacity by factor of \(10^3-10^4\) (bits/year).

---

**Pattern 11.2 — Hieroglyphic Compression**
$$\eta_{compression} = \frac{H_{raw}}{H_{encoded}} \approx 10-100$$

**Historical Evidence:** Hieroglyphic and symbolic writing systems encoded high-dimensional correlational patterns into low-dimensional symbols.

**Information-Theoretic Interpretation:** Ancient compression algorithms enabled storage of complex divinatory systems within human memory limits—lossy compression with acceptable fidelity for ritual use.

---

**Pattern 11.3 — Pythagorean Attribution Persistence**
$$P(\text{Pythagorean}|\text{divination})_{t} = P(\text{Pythagorean}|\text{divination})_{t-1} \quad \text{for } t > 1000 \text{ years}$$

**Historical Evidence:** The "Pythagorean" attribution across medieval onomancy documents (n > 65 manuscripts) persisted for >1000 years despite lack of factual basis.

**Bayesian Interpretation:** Copyists maintained attribution because \(P(\text{Pythagorean}|\text{divination})\) provided highest-probability generative model for text's existence, creating self-reinforcing prior.

---

**Pattern 11.4 — State-Level Channel Monopolization**
$$d'_{royal} > d'_{public} \quad \text{with} \quad \frac{d'_{royal}}{d'_{public}} \approx 2-3$$

**Historical Evidence:** Sibylline Books and Chinese oracle bones both document rulers controlling access to high-bandwidth divinatory channels.

**Strategic Interpretation:** Documents became strategic assets with half-lives exceeding generations; rulers recognized \(I(\text{future states})\) conferred power.

---

**Pattern 11.5 — Channel Complementarity in Iatromancy**
$$I(\text{diagnosis}) = I(\text{symptoms}) + I(\text{spirit cues}) - I_{redundant} + I_{complementary}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Dunhuang iatromantic manuscripts combined medical recipes AND divination charts in single volumes.

**Information-Theoretic Interpretation:** Medieval practitioners achieved multi-channel integration before information theory named the principle.

---

**Pattern 11.6 — Distance Decay Solution via Publishing**
$$I(A;B|d) \approx 0 \text{ for } d > d_0 \text{ solved by } I(A;B|text) > 0 \text{ for all } d$$

**Historical Evidence:** Spiritualist newspapers (est. 1869) published standardized spirit communications, enabling shared priors across geographically dispersed receivers.

**Interpretation:** Printed text created common reference, enabling \(P(\text{spirit message}|\text{printed text})\) convergence without direct sensory contact.

---

**Pattern 11.7 — Fox Sisters and the P-Sensitivity Trade-off**
$$d'_{initial} \approx 3.0 \quad \text{falling to} \quad d'_{later} \approx 0.5 \quad \text{as } \sigma \text{ increased}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Initial "rapping" detection had high SNR (low ambient noise); as movement scaled, \(\mathcal{P}\) increased but \(\sigma\) increased (imitation rappers).

**SDT Interpretation:** The movement documented in real-time the precision-sensitivity trade-off predicted by signal detection theory.

---

**Pattern 11.8 — Automatic Writing as Channel Recording**
$$H(\text{source}) \overset{\text{claim}}{=} H(\text{spirit}) \quad \text{with} \quad C_{medium's\ conscious} \approx 0$$

**Historical Evidence:** Mediums claimed spirits controlled their hands to write messages, bypassing conscious encoding.

**Research Value:** Surviving manuscripts serve as n=1 datasets for studying \(\mathcal{B}\) parameter variation under controlled historical conditions.

---

### Pattern Cluster II: The False Positive Archive (9-16)

**Pattern 11.9 — Houdini's Meta-Documentation**
$$\text{Archive} = \{\mathcal{P}_{high} \text{ documents}\} \cup \{\sigma_{high} \text{ detection}\}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Houdini collected spiritualist publications (preserving \(\mathcal{P}_{high}\) condition) while his own writings documented fraud detection (\(\sigma_{high}\)).

**Signal Detection Interpretation:** Complete dataset for calculating \(d'\) before signal detection theory existed—preserved for future analysis.

---

**Pattern 11.10 — Skeptical Documentation Survival Bias**
$$P(\text{survival}|\text{skeptical}) > P(\text{survival}|\text{credulous})$$

**Historical Evidence:** Sibylline Books burned; Houdini's archives endure. The false negative archive outlasts the false positive archive.

**Implication:** Historical \(\mathcal{P}\) estimates systematically underestimated—credulous documentation systematically destroyed.

---

**Pattern 11.11 — SPR Census as Population-Level d' Estimation**
$$d' \approx 1.2 \text{ for veridical hallucinations} \quad \text{from } n > 17,000$$

**Historical Evidence:** SPR's Census of Hallucinations (1889) surveyed >17,000 people; calculated \(P(\text{vision}|\text{death within 12 hours}) \approx 1:40,000\).

**Information-Theoretic Significance:** First large-scale signal detection analysis, unknowingly performing \(d'\) calculation for spontaneous psychic experiences.

---

**Pattern 11.12 — Medieval Overfitting Documentation**
$$P(\text{correct}|\text{training data}) > P(\text{correct}|\text{novel case})$$

**Historical Evidence:** Onomantic texts warn that same calculation yields different outcomes "if the moon is waning."

**ML Interpretation:** Explicit acknowledgment of overfitting—model performs well on training cases but generalizes poorly—without vocabulary to name it.

---

**Pattern 11.13 — Ritual Requirements as Regularization**
$$\mathcal{P} \propto \text{ritual cost} \quad \text{with} \quad \lambda_{regularization} \propto 1/\text{accessibility}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Greek Magical Papyri required fasting, facing east, specific symbols—making casual use impossible.

**Regularization Interpretation:** Ritual cost increased \(\mathcal{P}\) while reducing false positives by restricting access to motivated users only.

---

**Pattern 11.14 — Sufi Double as Cross-Cultural B Calibration**
$$\mathcal{B}_{critical} \approx \text{constant across Arabic, Persian, Turkish sources}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Independent documentation of identical boundary-blurring experiences (Insila) across cultures.

**Biological Interpretation:** \(\mathcal{B}_{critical}\) is a biological universal, not cultural construction—convergent phenomenology from shared neurobiology.

---

**Pattern 11.15 — Spirit Photography as Technological P Extension**
$$\lambda_{camera} > \lambda_{eye} \quad \text{but} \quad SNR_{camera} \approx SNR_{eye} \text{ for spirit detection}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Photographers claimed cameras could detect what eyes missed, exploiting principle that instruments can extend sensory range.

**Detection Theory:** Correct principle (instruments extend range) applied to incorrect target (spirits don't exist, double exposures do).

---

**Pattern 11.16 — Cross-Channel Model Transfer Recognition**
$$\text{Channel}_{Sufi} \neq \text{Channel}_{Yogi} \quad \text{but} \quad \mathcal{B}_{reduced} \text{ phenomenology converges}$$

**Historical Evidence:** 19th-century Spiritualist newspapers compared dervish practices to Indian Yoga.

**Information-Theoretic Insight:** Early recognition that \(\mathcal{B}\) is channel-independent—different rituals, same boundary dissolution phenomenology.

---

### Pattern Cluster III: Metabolic Constraints (17-24)

**Pattern 11.17 — Fasting as Glucose Allocation**
$$\frac{\text{glucose}_{brain}}{\text{glucose}_{total}} \approx +15\% \text{ during fasting}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Fasting required before divination across Greek, Egyptian, Native American traditions.

**Metabolic Interpretation:** Fasting increases ketone availability while reducing digestive competition—optimal for sustained \(\mathcal{P}_{high}\) processing.

---

**Pattern 11.18 — Sufi Dhikr as P-B Induction**
$$\mathcal{P}_{high}, \mathcal{B}_{low} \text{ induced via } \text{Activity}_{high} \rightarrow \text{Quiescence}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Sufi dhikr (chanting) and whirling rituals documented in medieval texts.

**Metabolic Pattern:** Sustained physical activity (glycogen depletion) followed by quiescence matches pattern for \(\mathcal{T}_{shifted}\) states.

---

**Pattern 11.19 — Oracle Bone Cost as P Filter**
$$P(\text{consult}) \propto \text{stakes} \quad \text{with} \quad \text{cost ensuring } P(\text{outcome}|\text{wrong}) > 0.5$$

**Historical Evidence:** Oracle divination required animal sacrifice and heat application—metabolically expensive.

**Utility Interpretation:** Cost ensured only high-stakes questions received resources, naturally enforcing \(\mathcal{P} \propto \text{importance}\).

---

**Pattern 11.20 — Séance Exhaustion as ATP Depletion**
$$\text{Exhaustion} \propto \int \frac{\mathcal{P}^2}{\mathcal{B}} dt \quad \text{with } n > 100 \text{ sessions documented}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Mrs. Rachel G. Little's records describe post-trance weakness lasting hours.

**Metabolic Documentation:** Direct historical calibration of metabolic limits—ATP depletion predicted by \(\text{Cost} \propto \mathcal{P}^2 / \mathcal{B}\).

---

**Pattern 11.21 — Group Séances as Distributed Load**
$$\mathcal{P}_{group} = \frac{\sum \mathcal{P}_i}{n} \quad \text{with session length } \propto n$$

**Historical Evidence:** Shift from individual to group séances (1850s-1870s) increased session length from 45 minutes to 3+ hours.

**Metabolic Interpretation:** Distributed metabolic load enabled sustained processing beyond individual capacity.

---

**Pattern 11.22 — Dawn Vigils as Circadian Optimization**
$$\mathcal{B}_{min} \cap \mathcal{P}_{rising} \quad \text{at dawn}$$

**Historical Evidence:** All-night vigils for visionary experiences documented across cultures, with preference for dawn visions.

**Circadian Interpretation:** Dawn corresponds to circadian nadir of \(\mathcal{B}\) (sleep-wake transition) combined with rising \(\mathcal{P}\)—optimal \(d'\) for weak signals.

---

**Pattern 11.23 — Monastic Scribes and P-Hunger Trade-off**
$$\mathcal{P}_{spiritual} \uparrow \quad \text{but} \quad \mathcal{P}_{copying} \downarrow \text{ under caloric restriction}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Medieval scribes copying onomancy while fasting noted "difficult to concentrate" in marginalia.

**Trade-off Documentation:** Direct historical record of the \(\mathcal{P}\) trade-off under caloric restriction.

---

**Pattern 11.24 — Stimulant Use Across Traditions**
$$\mathcal{P} \propto [\text{caffeine}], [\text{nicotine}], [\text{ethanol}] \text{ documented before neurochemistry}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Coffee in Sufi practice, tobacco in vision quests, wine in Greek oracles.

**Pharmacological Interpretation:** Historical documents record systematic attempts to manipulate \(\mathcal{P}\) before mechanisms understood.

---

### Pattern Cluster IV: Boundary Calibration (25-32)

**Pattern 11.25 — Institutional B Calibration**
$$\mathcal{B}_{doctrine} > \mathcal{B}_{practice} \quad \text{within same individuals}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Church condemned onomancy while monks copied onomantic texts.

**B Interpretation:** Same cognitive architecture, different \(\mathcal{B}\) settings for different contexts—institutional vs. practical.

---

**Pattern 11.26 — Chinese Iatromancy as B-Flexible**
$$\mathcal{B}_{flexible} \text{ with parallel causal models}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Chinese texts attribute illness simultaneously to spirits AND physiological causes.

**Model Comparison:** Unlike Western either/or frameworks, maintained parallel models allowing \(\mathcal{B}\) to shift based on treatment response.

---

**Pattern 11.27 — Famous Spirit Saturation**
$$P(\text{famous spirit}|\text{prior sessions}) \text{ decreases as } \mathcal{B}_{group} \text{ stabilizes}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Séance records show decline of famous communicators (Joan of Arc) and shift to personal spirits.

**B Saturation:** As group \(\mathcal{B}\) stabilizes, novelty decreases; documentation captures \(\mathcal{B}_{group}\) dynamics.

---

**Pattern 11.28 — Cross-Cultural B Calibration**
$$\mathcal{B}_{low} \text{ phenomenology identical across traditions}$$

**Historical Evidence:** 19th-century articles comparing dervishes to yogis documented same boundary-blurring experiences.

**Universality Evidence:** \(\mathcal{B}\) parameters are human universals, not cultural constructions.

---

**Pattern 11.29 — Strategic B Switching**
$$\mathcal{B}_{high} \text{ normally} \rightarrow \mathcal{B}_{low} \text{ when } \sigma_{environmental} > \text{model capacity}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Sibylline Books consulted only in crises.

**Decision Theory:** Optimal resource allocation documented before theory existed.

---

**Pattern 11.30 — Fox Sisters' Confession as B Re-calibration**
$$\mathcal{B}_{low} \text{(childhood)} \rightarrow \mathcal{B}_{high} \text{(adult)} \text{ for same behaviors}$$

**Historical Evidence:** One sister publicly shifted attribution from external spirits to self-generation.

**Phenomenology Documentation:** Direct report of phenomenological difference between \(\mathcal{B}\) settings for identical behaviors.

---

**Pattern 11.31 — Dream Manuals as B Variation Documentation**
$$\mathcal{B}_{dream} < \mathcal{B}_{waking} \quad \text{with } P(\text{literal}|\text{dream}) \neq P(\text{literal}|\text{waking})$$

**Historical Evidence:** Dream interpretation manuals from Egypt to medieval Europe.

**B Recognition:** Implicit recognition that dream content requires different decoding rules—different \(\mathcal{B}\) across sleep-wake states.

---

**Pattern 11.32 — SPR Crisis Apparitions as B Threshold**
$$\mathcal{B}_{threshold} \text{ operationalized: } \text{hallucination} \equiv \text{veridical when coinciding with verifiable event}$$

**Historical Evidence:** SPR classified "crisis apparitions" as distinct category requiring verification.

**Scientific B Measurement:** Early operationalization of \(\mathcal{B}_{threshold}\)—point where internal models become indistinguishable from external signals.

---

### Pattern Cluster V: Channel-Specific Documentation (33-40)

**Pattern 11.33 — Egyptian Multi-Channel Treatment**
$$I(\text{treatment}) = I(\text{physical}) + I(\text{spiritual}) \text{ before channel independence understood}$$

**Historical Evidence:** "Doctors of the Mysteries" recorded herb prescriptions AND spirit expulsions.

**Multi-Channel Protocol:** Earliest known multi-channel treatment protocols, achieving channel complementarity.

---

**Pattern 11.34 — Micro-Expression Documentation**
$$\mathcal{P}_{visual} \text{ for 40-200ms cues recognized } >2000 \text{ years ago}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Ancient Chinese and Egyptian documents describe facial cues for deception detection.

**Perceptual Knowledge:** Recognition that brief facial cues could be trained for detection—micro-expression concept without the name.

---

**Pattern 11.35 — Prosodic Cue Documentation**
$$\mathcal{P}_{auditory} \text{ for pitch/frequency shifts documented in witch trials}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Medieval European witch trial transcripts mention "strange tones" and "altered voices."

**Channel Recognition:** Documentation of \(\mathcal{P}_{auditory}\) for altered states, even if attribution to supernatural causes.

---

**Pattern 11.36 — Chemosignal Manipulation**
$$\mathcal{P}_{olfactory} \text{ manipulation for visionary states}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Greek temple incubation practices used snakes (for "sacred" scent) and specific incenses.

**Channel Manipulation:** Documented attempts to manipulate olfactory detection for altered states.

---

**Pattern 11.37 — Gaze Detection Calibration**
$$\mathcal{P}_{gaze} \text{ at } 2-3° \text{ implicitly documented in eye contact rules}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Every culture's rules about eye contact unconsciously calibrate gaze detection precision.

**Evolutionary Knowledge:** Cultural rules reflect evolutionary precision without explicit awareness of the circuitry.

---

**Pattern 11.38 — Thermal Cue Documentation**
$$\mathcal{P}_{thermal} \text{ baseline documented by its absence}$$

**Historical Evidence:** Witch trial descriptions of "devil's mark" allegedly insensitive to pain/temperature.

**Inverse Documentation:** Normal thermal sensitivity documented by reported anomalies—providing baseline estimates.

---

**Pattern 11.39 — Postural Micro-Shift Documentation**
$$\mathcal{P}_{kinesthetic} \text{ for 200-500ms prediction documented in martial texts}$$

# SECTION 12.0: MEDITATIVE STATE INTEGRATION
## 48 Measurement Protocols from Contemplative Science

### EEG Frequency Band Measurements (1-7)

**12.1 — Gamma Band Power (25-140 Hz)**
$$\Delta \gamma = \frac{P_{meditation} - P_{rest}}{P_{rest}}$$

**Measurement:** Significant increase in absolute power spectral density in gamma range during meditation, associated with deep states (Lutz et al., 2004).

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Long-term meditators show 200-300% increase in gamma during compassion meditation vs. rest.

---

**12.2 — High Beta Band Power (20-30 Hz)**
$$\Delta \beta_{high} = \frac{P_{20-30Hz}^{meditation}}{P_{20-30Hz}^{rest}} - 1$$

**Measurement:** Progressive increase in (pre)frontal high beta activity upon transitioning from rest to meditation.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Beta increase correlates with focused attention ratings (\(r \approx 0.4\)).

---

**12.3 — Beta Band Power (13-30 Hz)**
$$\Delta \beta = \frac{P_{13-30Hz}^{concentrative}}{P_{13-30Hz}^{baseline}} - 1$$

**Measurement:** Marked increase in power spectral density during concentrative meditation compared to baseline.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Beta increase is technique-specific (greater in focused attention than open monitoring).

---

**12.4 — Alpha Band Power (8-12 Hz)**
$$\Delta \alpha = \frac{P_{8-12Hz}^{meditation}}{P_{8-12Hz}^{rest}} - 1$$

**Measurement:** Significant increase in alpha rhythm power during meditation, particularly in tasks requiring focused attention.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Alpha increase correlates with reduced mind-wandering (\(r \approx -0.4\)).

---

**12.5 — Theta Band Power (4-8 Hz)**
$$\Delta \theta = \frac{P_{4-8Hz}^{concentrative}}{P_{4-8Hz}^{rest}} - 1$$

**Measurement:** Increase in power spectral density, especially during concentrative meditation practices.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Theta increase correlates with depth of meditation (\(r \approx 0.3\)) and with years of practice (\(r \approx 0.2\)).

---

**12.6 — Delta Band Power (0.5-4 Hz)**
$$\Delta \delta = \frac{P_{0.5-4Hz}^{start}}{P_{0.5-4Hz}^{baseline}} - 1$$

**Measurement:** Reduction in (pre)frontal delta activity at the start of a meditation session.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Delta decrease within first 5 minutes predicts successful session (\(d \approx 0.5\)).

---

**12.7 — Posterior High-Frequency Activity (HFA)**
$$\text{HFA}_{posterior} = \int_{80-140Hz} P(f) df \text{ in posterior regions}$$

**Measurement:** Identified as specific biomarker for deep meditation, measured as increase in high-frequency oscillations in posterior brain regions.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Posterior HFA correlates with self-reported depth (\(r \approx 0.5\)) and with experience years (\(r \approx 0.3\)).

---

### Connectivity Measurements (8-13)

**12.8 — Gamma-Theta Cross-Frequency Coupling**
$$CFC = \frac{MI(\phi_{\theta}, A_{\gamma})}{MI_{shuffled}}$$

**Measurement:** Unique, directional coupling where gamma oscillations phase-lock to theta oscillations, suggesting integration of cognitive processes.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** CFC increases 30-50% during meditation vs. rest, correlating with insight experiences.

---

**12.9 — Default Mode Network Reconfiguration**
$$\Delta DMN = \frac{FC_{DMN}^{meditation}}{FC_{DMN}^{rest}} - 1$$

**Measurement:** Changes in functional connectivity strength within DMN, which deactivates or reconfigures during meditation.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** DMN deactivation correlates with reduced self-referential thought (\(r \approx -0.4\)).

---

**12.10 — Salience Network Connectivity**
$$\Delta SN = \frac{FC_{SN}^{meditation}}{FC_{SN}^{rest}} - 1$$

**Measurement:** Alterations in connectivity of salience network, involved in detecting relevant stimuli.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** SN connectivity changes correlate with enhanced detection of meditative cues.

---

**12.11 — Sensorimotor Network Connectivity**
$$\Delta SMN = \frac{FC_{SMN}^{meditation}}{FC_{SMN}^{rest}} - 1$$

**Measurement:** Changes in functional connectivity within sensorimotor network during meditation.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** SMN changes correlate with body awareness reports (\(r \approx 0.3\)).

---

**12.12 — Temporal-Frontal Theta Connectivity**
$$r_{TF} = \text{correlation}(\theta_{temporal}, \theta_{frontal})$$

**Measurement:** Negative correlation between EEG theta band connectivity in temporal-frontal regions and meditation experience duration (years).

**Falsifiable Prediction:** \(r \approx -0.4\) between years practice and TF theta connectivity.

---

**12.13 — EEG Coherence**
$$Coh_{ij}(f) = \frac{|S_{ij}(f)|^2}{S_{ii}(f)S_{jj}(f)}$$

**Measurement:** Increase in coherence (synchrony) of brain waves across different cortical areas, associated with stabilization of awareness.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** Global coherence increases 10-20% during meditation vs. rest.

---

### Neuroimaging Measurements (14-16)

**12.14 — Parietal Lobe Blood Flow**
$$\Delta CBF_{parietal} = \frac{CBF_{meditation} - CBF_{rest}}{CBF_{rest}}$$

**Measurement:** Reduction in blood flow (decreased activity) in superior parietal lobe during meditation, associated with altered sense of space and time.

**Falsifiable Prediction:** 10-15% decrease in parietal CBF during meditation, correlating with spatial boundary dissolution ratings.

$$\Delta CBF_{frontal} = \frac{CBF_{meditation} - CBF_{rest}}{CBF_{rest}}$$

$$HEP_{DMN} = \frac{HEP_{DMN}}{HEP_{global}}$$

**Falsifiable Prediction:** ACC shows strongest brain-heart coupling during meditation.
