# SECTION 13.0: CODE LIBRARY
## 144 Python Functions for Hyper-Correlational Processing

### Group 1 — Statistical Foundation (Functions 1-18)

```python
# Function 1: Wilcoxon Signed-Rank Test for Psychic Accuracy
def calc_wilcoxon_accuracy(data_psychic, chance=0.5):
    """
    H0: median accuracy = 0.5 (chance)
    test: scipy.stats.wilcoxon(data_psychic - 0.5)
    output: W-statistic, p-value, effect size r = Z / sqrt(N)
    requirement: N >= 100; pre-registered; Bonferroni correction
    """
    from scipy.stats import wilcoxon
    import numpy as np
    
    data = np.array(data_psychic) - chance
    result = wilcoxon(data)
    Z = result.zstatistic
    r = Z / np.sqrt(len(data_psychic))
    
    return {'W': result.statistic, 'p': result.pvalue, 'r': r}


# Function 2: Cohen's d with Bootstrap CI
def compute_cohens_d(group_a, group_b, paired=False, n_bootstrap=10000):
    """
    d = (mean_a - mean_b) / pooled_std
    pooled_std = sqrt(((n_a-1)*std_a^2 + (n_b-1)*std_b^2) / (n_a+n_b-2))
    95% CI via bootstrap
    minimum N: G*Power for d=0.5, power=0.8, alpha=0.05 -> N=64 per group
    """
    import numpy as np
    from scipy import stats
    
    n_a, n_b = len(group_a), len(group_b)
    mean_a, mean_b = np.mean(group_a), np.mean(group_b)
    std_a, std_b = np.std(group_a, ddof=1), np.std(group_b, ddof=1)
    
    pooled_std = np.sqrt(((n_a-1)*std_a**2 + (n_b-1)*std_b**2) / (n_a+n_b-2))
    d = (mean_a - mean_b) / pooled_std
    
    # Bootstrap CI
    boot_d = []
    combined = np.concatenate([group_a, group_b])
    for _ in range(n_bootstrap):
        boot_a = np.random.choice(combined, n_a, replace=True)
        boot_b = np.random.choice(combined, n_b, replace=True)
        boot_d.append(compute_cohens_d(boot_a, boot_b, paired=False, 
                                      n_bootstrap=1)[0])
    
    ci_lower, ci_upper = np.percentile(boot_d, [2.5, 97.5])
    
    return d, ci_lower, ci_upper


# Function 3: Mutual Information via KSG Estimator
def compute_mutual_information_ksg(X, Y, k=3, n_shuffles=200, units='bits'):
    """
    Kraskov-Stogbauer-Grassberger k-nearest-neighbor estimator
    Bias correction: subtract MI(X_shuffled, Y) from 200 shuffles
    Units: bits (log2) or nats (ln)
    Output: MI ± SE, 95% CI, p-value from permutation test
    """
    from sklearn.feature_selection import mutual_info_regression
    import numpy as np
    
    X = np.array(X).reshape(-1, 1)
    Y = np.array(Y)
    
    # Compute MI
    mi = mutual_info_regression(X, Y, n_neighbors=k)[0]
    
    # Shuffle test
    mi_shuffled = []
    for _ in range(n_shuffles):
        Y_shuff = np.random.permutation(Y)
        mi_shuffled.append(mutual_info_regression(X, Y_shuff, 
                                                  n_neighbors=k)[0])
    
    mi_corrected = mi - np.mean(mi_shuffled)
    p_value = np.mean(np.array(mi_shuffled) >= mi)
    ci_lower, ci_upper = np.percentile(mi_shuffled, [2.5, 97.5])
    
    if units == 'bits':
        conversion = 1.0 / np.log(2)
    else:  # nats
        conversion = 1.0
    
    return {'MI': mi_corrected * conversion,
            'SE': np.std(mi_shuffled) * conversion,
            'CI': (ci_lower * conversion, ci_upper * conversion),
            'p': p_value}


# Function 4: Spectral Radius from MVAR
def estimate_spectral_radius_mvar(eeg_data, model_order='AIC'):
    """
    1. Select MVAR model order p via AIC minimization
    2. Fit MVAR: X(t) = Σ_{k=1}^{p} A_k·X(t-k) + ε(t)
    3. Stack coefficient matrices into companion matrix
    4. ρ = max |eigenvalues(companion matrix)|
    5. Stationarity check: ADF test on all channels (p < 0.05)
    """
    import numpy as np
    from statsmodels.tsa.api import VAR
    from statsmodels.tsa.stattools import adfuller
    
    # Check stationarity
    for ch in range(eeg_data.shape[1]):
        p_val = adfuller(eeg_data[:, ch])[1]
        if p_val > 0.05:
            raise ValueError(f"Channel {ch} non-stationary (p={p_val})")
    
    # Fit VAR model
    model = VAR(eeg_data)
    if model_order == 'AIC':
        order = model.select_order(maxlags=20).selected_orders['aic']
    else:
        order = model_order
    
    results = model.fit(order)
    
    # Build companion matrix
    k = eeg_data.shape[1]  # number of channels
    A = np.zeros((k*order, k*order))
    for i in range(order):
        A[:k, i*k:(i+1)*k] = results.coefs[i].T
    
    for i in range(1, order):
        A[i*k:(i+1)*k, (i-1)*k:i*k] = np.eye(k)
    
    # Compute spectral radius
    eigenvalues = np.linalg.eigvals(A)
    rho = np.max(np.abs(eigenvalues))
    
    return rho, order


# Function 5: Source Localization with LCMV Beamforming
def source_localize_lcmv(raw_eeg, forward_model, noise_cov):
    """
    Linearly Constrained Minimum Variance beamforming
    Input: raw EEG data, forward model (lead field matrix), noise covariance
    Output: source-localized time series
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    # Compute data covariance
    data_cov = np.cov(raw_eeg.T)
    
    # Regularize
    data_cov_reg = data_cov + 0.01 * np.eye(data_cov.shape[0]) * np.trace(data_cov)
    
    n_sources = forward_model.shape[1]
    source_data = np.zeros((n_sources, raw_eeg.shape[0]))
    
    for i in range(n_sources):
        L = forward_model[:, i:i+1]
        
        # LCMV filter
        W = np.linalg.solve(data_cov_reg, L)
        W = W / np.dot(L.T, W)
        
        # Apply filter
        source_data[i, :] = np.dot(W.T, raw_eeg.T).flatten()
    
    return source_data.T


# Function 6: Phase-Locking Value with Surrogate Correction
def compute_phase_locking_value(signal_a, signal_b, freq_band, fs, 
                                n_surrogates=200):
    """
    1. Bandpass filter to freq_band (4th-order Butterworth)
    2. Hilbert transform -> analytic signal -> instantaneous phase
    3. PLV = |mean(exp(i·(phase_a - phase_b)))|
    4. Surrogate correction: PLV_true = PLV_raw - mean(PLV_shuffled)
    5. Statistical test: permutation, p < 0.01 threshold
    """
    from scipy.signal import butter, filtfilt, hilbert
    import numpy as np
    
    # Bandpass filter
    nyquist = fs / 2
    low, high = freq_band[0] / nyquist, freq_band[1] / nyquist
    b, a = butter(4, [low, high], btype='band')
    
    sig_a_filt = filtfilt(b, a, signal_a)
    sig_b_filt = filtfilt(b, a, signal_b)
    
    # Hilbert transform for phase
    phase_a = np.angle(hilbert(sig_a_filt))
    phase_b = np.angle(hilbert(sig_b_filt))
    
    # Raw PLV
    phase_diff = phase_a - phase_b
    plv_raw = np.abs(np.mean(np.exp(1j * phase_diff)))
    
    # Surrogate correction
    plv_surrogates = []
    for _ in range(n_surrogates):
        # Phase-randomized surrogates
        phase_a_shuff = np.random.permutation(phase_a)
        phase_diff_shuff = phase_a_shuff - phase_b
        plv_surrogates.append(np.abs(np.mean(np.exp(1j * phase_diff_shuff))))
    
    plv_corrected = plv_raw - np.mean(plv_surrogates)
    p_value = np.mean(np.array(plv_surrogates) >= plv_raw)
    
    return plv_corrected, p_value


# Function 7: Holm-Bonferroni Correction
def apply_bonferroni_holm_correction(p_values, alpha=0.05):
    """
    Holm-Bonferroni step-down procedure
    Sort p-values ascending; compare to alpha/(m - k + 1) for k-th ranked
    Less conservative than Bonferroni; controls family-wise error rate
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    m = len(p_values)
    sorted_idx = np.argsort(p_values)
    sorted_p = p_values[sorted_idx]
    
    rejected = np.zeros(m, dtype=bool)
    
    for k, p in enumerate(sorted_p):
        if p <= alpha / (m - k):
            rejected[sorted_idx[k]] = True
        else:
            break
    
    return rejected


# Function 8: Bootstrap Confidence Interval
def bootstrap_confidence_interval(data, statistic_fn, iterations=10000, ci=0.95):
    """
    Resample with replacement iterations times
    Apply statistic_fn to each resample
    CI: percentile method (2.5th, 97.5th percentile of bootstrap distribution)
    Bias correction: BCA if skewness > 0.5
    """
    import numpy as np
    from scipy.stats import skew
    
    n = len(data)
    boot_stats = []
    
    for _ in range(iterations):
        boot_sample = np.random.choice(data, n, replace=True)
        boot_stats.append(statistic_fn(boot_sample))
    
    boot_stats = np.array(boot_stats)
    
    # Percentile CI
    lower = np.percentile(boot_stats, (1-ci)/2 * 100)
    upper = np.percentile(boot_stats, (1+ci)/2 * 100)
    
    # Bias correction if needed
    if abs(skew(boot_stats)) > 0.5:
        # Simple bias-corrected accelerated (BCA) placeholder
        # Full implementation would include acceleration factor
        z0 = np.sum(boot_stats < statistic_fn(data)) / iterations
        lower = np.percentile(boot_stats, 100 * z0)
        upper = np.percentile(boot_stats, 100 * (1 - z0))
    
    return statistic_fn(data), (lower, upper)


# Function 9: Power Analysis for Required N
def power_analysis_required_n(effect_size, power=0.8, alpha=0.05, 
                              test='two-sample-t'):
    """
    Uses statsmodels.stats.power module
    Returns minimum N per group for specified parameters
    Must be called BEFORE data collection and reported in pre-registration
    For r: N = (z_{1-alpha/2} + z_{1-beta})^2 / (0.5·ln((1+r)/(1-r)))^2 + 3
    """
    from statsmodels.stats.power import TTestIndPower, TTestPower
    
    if test == 'two-sample-t':
        analysis = TTestIndPower()
        n = analysis.solve_power(effect_size=effect_size, power=power,
                                 alpha=alpha, ratio=1.0)
    elif test == 'paired-t':
        analysis = TTestPower()
        n = analysis.solve_power(effect_size=effect_size, power=power,
                                 alpha=alpha)
    elif test == 'correlation':
        import numpy as np
        from scipy.stats import norm
        
        z_alpha = norm.ppf(1 - alpha/2)
        z_beta = norm.ppf(power)
        n = ((z_alpha + z_beta) / (0.5 * np.log((1+effect_size)/(1-effect_size))))**2 + 3
    
    return int(np.ceil(n))


# Function 10: Higuchi Fractal Dimension
def extract_higuchi_fractal_dimension(signal, k_max=10):
    """
    Higuchi (1988) algorithm for 1D time series
    Output: D_f ∈ [1,2]; D_f ≈ 1.5 at criticality
    Units: dimensionless
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    n = len(signal)
    L = []
    k_values = range(1, k_max + 1)
    
    for k in k_values:
        Lk = []
        for m in range(k):
            Lmk = 0
            for i in range(1, int((n-m)/k)):
                Lmk += abs(signal[m + i*k] - signal[m + (i-1)*k])
            Lmk = Lmk * (n - 1) / (i * k * k)
            Lk.append(Lmk)
        L.append(np.mean(Lk))
    
    # Fit line to log(L) vs log(1/k)
    coeffs = np.polyfit(np.log(1.0/np.array(k_values)), np.log(L), 1)
    D_f = coeffs[0]
    
    return D_f


# Function 11: Transfer Entropy
def compute_transfer_entropy(source, target, lag=1, k=1, n_shuffles=200):
    """
    TE(X->Y) = H(Y_future|Y_past) - H(Y_future|Y_past, X_past)
    Estimator: KSG k-nearest-neighbor (bias corrected)
    Units: bits/sample
    Surrogate test: time-shifted nulls (N=200), p < 0.05
    """
    import numpy as np
    from sklearn.neighbors import NearestNeighbors
    
    n = len(source) - lag
    y_future = target[lag:]
    y_past = target[:n]
    x_past = source[:n]
    
    # Joint and marginal embeddings
    data_y = np.column_stack([y_past, y_future])
    data_yx = np.column_stack([y_past, x_past, y_future])
    
    # KSG estimator
    nbrs_y = NearestNeighbors(n_neighbors=k+1).fit(data_y)
    nbrs_yx = NearestNeighbors(n_neighbors=k+1).fit(data_yx)
    
    distances_y, _ = nbrs_y.kneighbors(data_y)
    distances_yx, _ = nbrs_yx.kneighbors(data_yx)
    
    epsilon_y = distances_y[:, -1]
    epsilon_yx = distances_yx[:, -1]
    
    # Count neighbors within epsilon
    te = 0
    for i in range(n):
        n_y = np.sum(np.linalg.norm(data_y - data_y[i], axis=1) <= epsilon_y[i]) - 1
        n_yx = np.sum(np.linalg.norm(data_yx - data_yx[i], axis=1) <= epsilon_yx[i]) - 1
        te += np.log(n_y / n_yx)
    
    te = te / n
    
    # Shuffle test
    te_shuffled = []
    for _ in range(n_shuffles):
        source_shuff = np.random.permutation(source)
        te_shuffled.append(compute_transfer_entropy(
            source_shuff, target, lag, k, n_shuffles=1)[0])
    
    p_value = np.mean(np.array(te_shuffled) >= te)
    
    return te, p_value


# Function 12: Cross-Frequency Coupling Modulation Index
def compute_cross_frequency_coupling_mi(phase_signal, amp_signal, 
                                        n_phase_bins=18):
    """
    Modulation Index (Tort et al., 2010)
    MI = KL(p_norm, p_uniform) / log(N_phase_bins)
    Normalized: MI ∈ [0, 1]
    Control: compute MI with phase-amplitude shuffled pairs
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    phase_bins = np.linspace(-np.pi, np.pi, n_phase_bins + 1)
    phase_indices = np.digitize(phase_signal, phase_bins) - 1
    
    # Mean amplitude per phase bin
    mean_amp = np.zeros(n_phase_bins)
    for i in range(n_phase_bins):
        mean_amp[i] = np.mean(amp_signal[phase_indices == i])
    
    # Normalize to probability distribution
    p_norm = mean_amp / np.sum(mean_amp)
    p_uniform = np.ones(n_phase_bins) / n_phase_bins
    
    # KL divergence
    kl = np.sum(p_norm * np.log(p_norm / p_uniform + 1e-10))
    mi = kl / np.log(n_phase_bins)
    
    return mi


# Function 13: Power-Law Avalanche Detection
def detect_avalanche_power_law(spike_counts, s_min=2):
    """
    Maximum likelihood estimation of τ (Clauset et al., 2009)
    τ = 1 + n · [∑ ln(s_i / s_min)]⁻¹
    Goodness of fit: KS test vs. power law; report D-statistic
    Compare to exponential alternative via likelihood ratio test
    """
    import numpy as np
    from scipy.stats import kstest, expon
    
    # Filter avalanches above minimum size
    s = spike_counts[spike_counts >= s_min]
    n = len(s)
    
    if n < 100:
        return None, None, None, None
    
    # MLE for power law exponent
    tau = 1 + n / np.sum(np.log(s / s_min))
    
    # KS test for power law fit
    # Generate power law samples with same parameters
    r = np.random.random(10000)
    s_sim = s_min * (1 - r) ** (-1/(tau-1))
    
    D_power, p_power = kstest(s, lambda x: (1 - (x/s_min)**(-(tau-1))) 
                                if x >= s_min else 0)
    
    # Fit exponential
    lambda_exp = 1 / np.mean(s)
    D_exp, p_exp = kstest(s, 'expon', args=(0, 1/lambda_exp))
    
    # Likelihood ratio test
    L_power = np.sum(np.log((tau-1)/s_min * (s/s_min)**(-tau)))
    L_exp = np.sum(np.log(lambda_exp * np.exp(-lambda_exp * s)))
    
    LR = L_power - L_exp
    
    return tau, D_power, LR, {'D_power': D_power, 'p_power': p_power,
                               'D_exp': D_exp, 'p_exp': p_exp}


# Function 14: Hurst Exponent via Detrended Fluctuation Analysis
def compute_hurst_exponent_dfa(ts, scales=None):
    """
    Detrended Fluctuation Analysis (Peng et al., 1994)
    H < 0.5 = anti-persistent; H = 0.5 = random; H > 0.5 = persistent
    H = 0.7 associated with criticality in EEG
    Scales: 10 log-spaced from 10 to N/4 samples
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    if scales is None:
        scales = np.logspace(np.log10(10), np.log10(len(ts)/4), 10).astype(int)
    
    # Integrate time series
    y = np.cumsum(ts - np.mean(ts))
    
    fluctuations = []
    for scale in scales:
        # Split into windows
        n_windows = len(y) // scale
        f2 = 0
        for v in range(n_windows):
            idx = np.arange(v*scale, (v+1)*scale)
            # Linear detrend
            coeffs = np.polyfit(idx, y[idx], 1)
            trend = np.polyval(coeffs, idx)
            f2 += np.sum((y[idx] - trend)**2)
        f2 = f2 / (n_windows * scale)
        fluctuations.append(np.sqrt(f2))
    
    # Fit line to log(fluctuation) vs log(scale)
    coeffs = np.polyfit(np.log(scales), np.log(fluctuations), 1)
    H = coeffs[0]
    
    return H


# Function 15: Sleep Spindle Analysis
def analyze_sleep_spindles(eeg_sleep, fs=256):
    """
    Bandpass: 12-15 Hz (sigma band)
    Detection: amplitude threshold > 2 SD above REM baseline
    Output: spindle count/hour, mean duration, mean amplitude
    """
    from scipy.signal import butter, filtfilt, hilbert
    import numpy as np
    
    # Bandpass filter for sigma band
    nyquist = fs / 2
    low, high = 12 / nyquist, 15 / nyquist
    b, a = butter(4, [low, high], btype='band')
    
    eeg_filt = filtfilt(b, a, eeg_sleep)
    
    # Hilbert envelope
    envelope = np.abs(hilbert(eeg_filt))
    
    # Threshold (2 SD above baseline)
    threshold = np.mean(envelope) + 2 * np.std(envelope)
    
    # Detect spindles
    above_thresh = envelope > threshold
    transitions = np.diff(np.concatenate([[0], above_thresh.astype(int), [0]]))
    starts = np.where(transitions == 1)[0]
    ends = np.where(transitions == -1)[0]
    
    durations = (ends - starts) / fs
    amplitudes = [np.max(envelope[s:e]) for s, e in zip(starts, ends)]
    
    # Filter for minimum duration (0.5 sec)
    valid = durations >= 0.5
    durations = durations[valid]
    amplitudes = np.array(amplitudes)[valid]
    starts = starts[valid]
    
    # Calculate metrics
    total_time = len(eeg_sleep) / fs / 3600  # hours
    count_per_hour = len(durations) / total_time
    mean_duration = np.mean(durations)
    mean_amplitude = np.mean(amplitudes)
    
    return {'count_per_hour': count_per_hour,
            'mean_duration': mean_duration,
            'mean_amplitude': mean_amplitude,
            'n_spindles': len(durations)}


# Function 16: Heart Rate Variability (RMSSD)
def measure_hrv_rmssd(rr_intervals):
    """
    RMSSD = sqrt(mean((RR_{i+1} - RR_i)^2))
    Units: milliseconds
    Minimum recording: 5 minutes of continuous ECG
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    rr = np.array(rr_intervals)
    diff = np.diff(rr)
    rmssd = np.sqrt(np.mean(diff**2))
    
    return rmssd


# Function 17: EEG Microstate Analysis
def perform_microstate_analysis(eeg_data, n_states=4, fs=None):
    """
    k-means clustering on EEG topographies at GFP peaks
    Optimal k: cross-validation + published norms (4-7 states)
    Output: state sequence, transition matrix, entropy rate
    """
    from sklearn.cluster import KMeans
    import numpy as np
    
    # Compute global field power
    gfp = np.std(eeg_data, axis=1)
    
    # Find GFP peaks
    from scipy.signal import find_peaks
    peaks, _ = find_peaks(gfp, distance=fs//10 if fs else 10)
    
    # Topographies at peaks
    topographies = eeg_data[peaks, :]
    
    # Cluster into microstates
    kmeans = KMeans(n_clusters=n_states, random_state=0, n_init=10)
    labels = kmeans.fit_predict(topographies)
    
    # Assign each time point to nearest microstate
    state_sequence = []
    for t in range(len(eeg_data)):
        dist = np.linalg.norm(eeg_data[t:t+1] - kmeans.cluster_centers_, axis=1)
        state_sequence.append(np.argmin(dist))
    
    state_sequence = np.array(state_sequence)
    
    # Transition matrix
    trans_mat = np.zeros((n_states, n_states))
    for i in range(len(state_sequence)-1):
        trans_mat[state_sequence[i], state_sequence[i+1]] += 1
    
    # Normalize
    trans_mat = trans_mat / trans_mat.sum(axis=1, keepdims=True)
    
    # Stationary distribution
    eigenvals, eigenvecs = np.linalg.eig(trans_mat.T)
    stationary = np.real(eigenvecs[:, np.argmin(np.abs(eigenvals - 1))])
    stationary = stationary / stationary.sum()
    
    # Entropy rate
    entropy_rate = -np.sum(stationary * np.sum(trans_mat * 
                                               np.log2(trans_mat + 1e-10), axis=1))
    
    return {'state_sequence': state_sequence,
            'transition_matrix': trans_mat,
            'entropy_rate': entropy_rate,
            'cluster_centers': kmeans.cluster_centers_}


# Function 18: Integrated Information (Φ)
def calculate_phi_iit(connectivity_matrix, method='PyPhi'):
    """
    Phi (Φ) = integrated information (Tononi et al., 2016)
    PyPhi library: Mayner et al. (2018)
    Computational limit: ~25 nodes; use for small networks or ROI-level
    Output: Φ in bits, MIP (minimum information partition)
    """
    # Note: Full PyPhi implementation would require complex setup
    # This is a simplified approximation using network measures
    
    import numpy as np
    
    # Normalize connectivity
    W = connectivity_matrix / np.max(np.abs(connectivity_matrix))
    
    # Approximate Φ via integration of information
    n = W.shape[0]
    
    # Mutual information between random bipartitions
    n_trials = 100
    phi_approx = 0
    
    for _ in range(n_trials):
        # Random partition
        part = np.random.choice([0, 1], n)
        if np.sum(part) == 0 or np.sum(part) == n:
            continue
        
        # Simplified integration measure
        within_A = W[np.ix_(part==0, part==0)]
        within_B = W[np.ix_(part==1, part==1)]
        between = W[np.ix_(part==0, part==1)]
        
        # Integration measure
        integration = (np.sum(np.abs(within_A)) + np.sum(np.abs(within_B))) / \
                     (np.sum(np.abs(between)) + 1)
        
        phi_approx = max(phi_approx, integration)
    
    return phi_approx
```

### Group 2 — Neural Signal Processing (Functions 19-36)

```python
# Function 19: Granger Causality
def compute_granger_causality(source, target, max_lag=10, criterion='aic'):
    """
    GC(X->Y) = ln(var(ε_Y|Y-past) / var(ε_Y|Y-past, X-past))
    Units: dimensionless (log variance ratio)
    """
    from statsmodels.tsa.api import VAR
    import numpy as np
    
    data = np.column_stack([source, target])
    
    # Fit unrestricted model (includes source)
    model_unrestricted = VAR(data)
    lag_order = model_unrestricted.select_order(maxlags=max_lag)
    if criterion == 'aic':
        p = lag_order.aic
    else:
        p = lag_order.bic
    
    results_unrestricted = model_unrestricted.fit(p)
    
    # Restricted model (target only)
    model_restricted = VAR(target.reshape(-1, 1))
    results_restricted = model_restricted.fit(p)
    
    # Residual variances
    resid_unrestricted = results_unrestricted.resid[:, 1]
    resid_restricted = results_restricted.resid.flatten()
    
    var_unrestricted = np.var(resid_unrestricted)
    var_restricted = np.var(resid_restricted)
    
    # Granger causality
    gc = np.log(var_restricted / var_unrestricted)
    
    # F-test for significance
    n = len(target) - p
    k = p  # number of parameters
    F = ((var_restricted - var_unrestricted) / k) / (var_unrestricted / (n - 2*k))
    p_value = 1 - stats.f.cdf(F, k, n - 2*k)
    
    return gc, p_value


# Function 20: Kuramoto Model for Dyadic Synchrony
def kuramoto_dyadic(frequencies, coupling, B_boundary, dt=0.001, T=10):
    """
    dθ_i/dt = ω_i + (K/(N·B)) Σ sin(θ_j - θ_i)
    Simulates phase coupling between oscillators
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    n_osc = len(frequencies)
    t = np.arange(0, T, dt)
    n_steps = len(t)
    
    phases = np.zeros((n_steps, n_osc))
    phases[0, :] = np.random.rand(n_osc) * 2 * np.pi
    
    K_eff = coupling / (n_osc * B_boundary)
    
    for i in range(1, n_steps):
        for j in range(n_osc):
            sin_sum = np.sum(np.sin(phases[i-1, :] - phases[i-1, j]))
            phases[i, j] = phases[i-1, j] + dt * (frequencies[j] + K_eff * sin_sum)
    
    # Compute order parameter
    r = np.abs(np.mean(np.exp(1j * phases), axis=1))
    
    return phases, r


# Function 21: Dynamic Causal Modeling (simplified)
def calculate_effective_connectivity_dcm(bold_data, design_matrix):
    """
    Simplified effective connectivity estimation
    Full DCM requires variational Bayesian inversion
    """
    import numpy as np
    from scipy.linalg import pinv
    
    # This is a placeholder for actual DCM
    # Full implementation would use SPM or similar
    
    # Simple correlation-based effective connectivity
    n_regions = bold_data.shape[1]
    effective_connectivity = np.zeros((n_regions, n_regions))
    
    for i in range(n_regions):
        for j in range(n_regions):
            if i != j:
                # Partial correlation controlling for other regions
                idx = [k for k in range(n_regions) if k not in [i, j]]
                if len(idx) > 0:
                    resid_i = bold_data[:, i] - bold_data[:, idx] @ \
                              pinv(bold_data[:, idx].T @ bold_data[:, idx]) @ \
                              bold_data[:, idx].T @ bold_data[:, i]
                    resid_j = bold_data[:, j] - bold_data[:, idx] @ \
                              pinv(bold_data[:, idx].T @ bold_data[:, idx]) @ \
                              bold_data[:, idx].T @ bold_data[:, j]
                    effective_connectivity[i, j] = np.corrcoef(resid_i, resid_j)[0, 1]
    
    return effective_connectivity


# Function 22: Betti Numbers via Persistent Homology
def find_betti_numbers(distance_matrix, max_dim=2):
    """
    Computes persistent homology of point cloud
    Returns Betti numbers β₀, β₁, β₂
    """
    # Note: Requires ripser or gudhi library
    # This is a placeholder
    
    try:
        from ripser import ripser
        from persim import plot_diagrams
        
        diagrams = ripser(distance_matrix, maxdim=max_dim)['dgms']
        
        # Count persistent features
        betti = []
        for dim in range(max_dim + 1):
            # Count features with persistence > threshold
            if dim < len(diagrams):
                persistence = diagrams[dim][:, 1] - diagrams[dim][:, 0]
                betti.append(np.sum(persistence > 0.1))
            else:
                betti.append(0)
        
        return betti
    
    except ImportError:
        print("Ripser not available. Using placeholder.")
        return [1, 0, 0]  # Placeholder


# Function 23: Avalanche Size Distribution
def detect_avalanche_size(spike_times, bin_size=0.001):
    """
    Measures distribution of neural "bursts" to check for power-law scaling
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    # Bin spike times
    max_time = np.max(spike_times)
    bins = np.arange(0, max_time + bin_size, bin_size)
    spike_counts, _ = np.histogram(spike_times, bins)
    
    # Detect avalanches (consecutive bins with spikes)
    active = spike_counts > 0
    transitions = np.diff(np.concatenate([[0], active.astype(int), [0]]))
    starts = np.where(transitions == 1)[0]
    ends = np.where(transitions == -1)[0]
    
    # Compute avalanche sizes
    avalanche_sizes = []
    for s, e in zip(starts, ends):
        avalanche_sizes.append(np.sum(spike_counts[s:e]))
    
    return np.array(avalanche_sizes)


# Function 24: PID Controller for Criticality
def optimize_pid_parameters(rho_target, rho_measured, dt, 
                           Kp_range=[0, 1], Ki_range=[0, 1], Kd_range=[0, 1]):
    """
    Find PID parameters that keep brain at edge of chaos
    """
    import numpy as np
    from scipy.optimize import minimize
    
    def pid_cost(params):
        Kp, Ki, Kd = params
        error = rho_target - rho_measured
        integral = np.cumsum(error) * dt
        derivative = np.diff(np.concatenate([[0], error])) / dt
        
        control = Kp * error + Ki * integral + Kd * derivative
        cost = np.mean((rho_target - (rho_measured + control))**2)
        return cost
    
    result = minimize(pid_cost, x0=[0.5, 0.1, 0.1],
                     bounds=[Kp_range, Ki_range, Kd_range])
    
    return result.x


# Function 25: Fourier Inversion for Memory Retrieval
def perform_fourier_inversion_memory(encoding_pattern, retrieval_cue):
    """
    Tests if retrieval matches 2D-FFT pattern of encoding state
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    # 2D Fourier transform of encoding pattern
    F_encoding = np.fft.fft2(encoding_pattern)
    
    # Retrieve via correlation in Fourier domain
    F_retrieved = np.fft.fft2(retrieval_cue) * np.conj(F_encoding)
    retrieved = np.fft.ifft2(F_retrieved)
    
    # Compare to actual memory
    similarity = np.corrcoef(retrieved.flatten(), encoding_pattern.flatten())[0, 1]
    
    return retrieved, similarity


# Function 26: Monte Carlo Permutation Test
def run_monte_carlo_permutation(data, n_permutations=10000):
    """
    Creates null distribution for any "psychic" hit rate
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    # Observed statistic
    observed = np.mean(data)
    
    # Permutation distribution
    permuted = []
    for _ in range(n_permutations):
        shuffled = np.random.permutation(data)
        permuted.append(np.mean(shuffled))
    
    permuted = np.array(permuted)
    p_value = np.mean(permuted >= observed)
    
    return observed, permuted, p_value


# Function 27: Variational Free Energy
def evaluate_variational_free_energy(observations, predictions, complexity):
    """
    F = Complexity - Accuracy
    """
    # Accuracy: negative log likelihood
    accuracy = -np.mean((observations - predictions)**2)
    
    # Free energy
    F = complexity - accuracy
    
    return F

    from sympy.physics.units import mass, length, time, current, temperature
    
    # Parse equation
    expr = sympify(equation_string)
    
    # Extract symbols and assign dimensions
    # This would need a comprehensive unit database
    
    # Placeholder
    return True


# Function 29: Cross-Frequency Coupling
def measure_cross_frequency_coupling(eeg_data, fs, f_phase=(4,8), f_amp=(30,80)):
    """
    Calculates Modulation Index (MI) between theta phase and gamma amplitude
    """
    from scipy.signal import butter, filtfilt, hilbert
    import numpy as np
    
    nyquist = fs / 2
    
    # Filter for phase frequency
    low_p, high_p = f_phase[0]/nyquist, f_phase[1]/nyquist
    b_p, a_p = butter(4, [low_p, high_p], btype='band')
    phase_signal = filtfilt(b_p, a_p, eeg_data)
    phase = np.angle(hilbert(phase_signal))
    
    # Filter for amplitude frequency
    low_a, high_a = f_amp[0]/nyquist, f_amp[1]/nyquist
    b_a, a_a = butter(4, [low_a, high_a], btype='band')
    amp_signal = filtfilt(b_a, a_a, eeg_data)
    amplitude = np.abs(hilbert(amp_signal))
    
    # Modulation Index
    n_bins = 18
    phase_bins = np.linspace(-np.pi, np.pi, n_bins + 1)
    phase_idx = np.digitize(phase, phase_bins) - 1
    
    mean_amp = np.zeros(n_bins)
    for i in range(n_bins):
        mean_amp[i] = np.mean(amplitude[phase_idx == i])
    
    p = mean_amp / np.sum(mean_amp)
    mi = (np.log(n_bins) + np.sum(p * np.log(p + 1e-10))) / np.log(n_bins)
    
    return mi


# Function 30: Critical Slowing Down Detection
def identify_critical_slowing_down(time_series, window_size=30):
    """
    Measures variance and autocorrelation increases before state transition
    """
    import numpy as np
    from scipy import stats
    
    n_windows = len(time_series) - window_size
    variance = np.zeros(n_windows)
    autocorr = np.zeros(n_windows)
    
    for i in range(n_windows):
        window = time_series[i:i+window_size]
        variance[i] = np.var(window)
        autocorr[i] = np.corrcoef(window[:-1], window[1:])[0, 1]
    
    # Test for increasing trend
    trend_var = stats.linregress(np.arange(n_windows), variance)
    trend_ac = stats.linregress(np.arange(n_windows), autocorr)
    
    return variance, autocorr, trend_var.slope, trend_ac.slope


# Function 31: Spectral Embedding for Polytope Visualization
def cluster_spectral_embedding(eeg_data, n_components=3):
    """
    Projects high-dimensional EEG into 3D manifold
    """
    from sklearn.manifold import SpectralEmbedding
    import numpy as np
    
    # Reshape: trials × features
    n_trials = eeg_data.shape[0]
    features = eeg_data.reshape(n_trials, -1)
    
    embedding = SpectralEmbedding(n_components=n_components)
    projected = embedding.fit_transform(features)
    
    return projected


# Function 32: Renyi Entropy
def calculate_renyi_entropy(data, alpha=2, base=2):
    """
    Generalized entropy measure: H_α = (1/(1-α)) log(∑ p_i^α)
    α=1: Shannon entropy; α=2: collision entropy
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    # Estimate probability distribution via histogram
    hist, _ = np.histogram(data, bins='auto', density=True)
    p = hist[hist > 0]
    
    if alpha == 1:
        # Shannon entropy (limit as α→1)
        H = -np.sum(p * np.log(p)) / np.log(base)
    else:
        # Renyi entropy
        H = (1/(1-alpha)) * np.log(np.sum(p**alpha)) / np.log(base)
    
    return H


# Function 33: Lindblad Master Equation Solver
def solve_lindblad_master_eq(H, L_list, rho0, t_span, gamma_list):
    """
    Models density matrix evolution under environment noise
    dρ/dt = -i[H,ρ] + Σ γ_k (L_k ρ L_k† - ½{L_k†L_k, ρ})
    """
    from scipy.integrate import solve_ivp
    import numpy as np
    
    n = H.shape[0]
    
    def lindblad_rhs(t, rho_vec):
        rho = rho_vec.reshape(n, n)
        
        # Unitary evolution
        drho = -1j * (H @ rho - rho @ H)
        
        # Dissipative terms
        for L, gamma in zip(L_list, gamma_list):
            L_dag = L.conj().T
            drho += gamma * (L @ rho @ L_dag - 0.5 * (L_dag @ L @ rho + rho @ L_dag @ L))
        
        return drho.flatten()
    
    rho0_vec = rho0.flatten()
    sol = solve_ivp(lindblad_rhs, t_span, rho0_vec, method='RK45')
    
    # Reshape solution
    rho_t = sol.y.T.reshape(-1, n, n)
    
    return sol.t, rho_t


# Function 34: Negentropy for Non-Gaussianity
def detect_non_gaussianity(signal):
    """
    Uses Negentropy to find "novel" signals in correlation substrate
    J(x) = H(x_gauss) - H(x)
    """
    from scipy.stats import entropy, norm
    import numpy as np
    
    # Estimate entropy of signal
    hist, bins = np.histogram(signal, bins='auto', density=True)
    H_signal = entropy(hist)
    
    # Entropy of Gaussian with same variance
    x_gauss = np.random.normal(0, np.std(signal), 10000)
    hist_gauss, _ = np.histogram(x_gauss, bins=bins, density=True)
    H_gauss = entropy(hist_gauss[hist_gauss > 0])
    
    # Negentropy
    J = H_gauss - H_signal
    
    return J


# Function 35: Ridge Regression for Reconstruction Fidelity
def run_ridge_regression_cv(X, y, alphas=None, cv_folds=5):
    """
    Tests reconstruction fidelity via cross-validation
    """
    from sklearn.linear_model import RidgeCV
    from sklearn.model_selection import cross_val_score
    import numpy as np
    
    if alphas is None:
        alphas = np.logspace(-3, 3, 10)
    
    # Ridge regression with CV
    model = RidgeCV(alphas=alphas, store_cv_values=True)
    model.fit(X, y)
    
    # Cross-validation scores
    cv_scores = cross_val_score(model, X, y, cv=cv_folds, scoring='r2')
    
    return {'best_alpha': model.alpha_,
            'best_score': model.best_score_,
            'cv_scores': cv_scores,
            'cv_mean': np.mean(cv_scores),
            'cv_std': np.std(cv_scores)}


# Function 36: Lyapunov Exponent
def analyze_lyapunov_exponent(trajectory, dt, n_steps=10, epsilon=1e-6):
    """
    Quantifies rate of divergence of nearby trajectories in P-B-T space
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    n = len(trajectory)
    d = trajectory.shape[1] if len(trajectory.shape) > 1 else 1
    
    if d == 1:
        trajectory = trajectory.reshape(-1, 1)
    
    lyapunov = 0
    n_valid = 0
    
    for i in range(n - n_steps * dt):
        # Reference point
        ref = trajectory[i]
        
        # Find nearest neighbor in state space
        distances = np.linalg.norm(trajectory - ref, axis=1)
        distances[i] = np.inf  # exclude self
        j = np.argmin(distances)
        
        if distances[j] < epsilon:
            continue
        
        # Track divergence
        d0 = distances[j]
        d1 = np.linalg.norm(trajectory[i + n_steps] - trajectory[j + n_steps])
        
        lyapunov += np.log(d1 / d0) / (n_steps * dt)
        n_valid += 1
    
    if n_valid > 0:
        lyapunov = lyapunov / n_valid
    
    return lyapunov
```

# Function 37: 7T MRS Protocol for ATP Measurement
def measure_atp_mrs(mrs_spectrum, calibration_factor, voxel_volume):
    """
    [ATP] = (³¹P MRS signal * calibration factor) / voxel_volume
    Units: mM
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    # Integrate ATP peak (around -2.5 ppm relative to PCr)
    # This is simplified; actual analysis uses specialized software
    
    atp_signal = np.trapz(mrs_spectrum)
    atp_concentration = (atp_signal * calibration_factor) / voxel_volume
    
    return atp_concentration


# Function 38: Hyperscanning EEG Synchronization
def hyperscanning_synchronize(eeg_a, eeg_b, lsl_data, max_jitter_ms=1):
    """
    Concurrent recording with dual-LSL clock synchronization
    Ensures <1ms jitter between systems
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    # Extract timestamps from LSL
    timestamps_a = lsl_data['timestamps_a']
    timestamps_b = lsl_data['timestamps_b']
    
    # Find matching time points
    matched_indices = []
    for i, t_a in enumerate(timestamps_a):
        # Find closest timestamp in B
        t_diff = np.abs(timestamps_b - t_a)
        j = np.argmin(t_diff)
        if t_diff[j] * 1000 < max_jitter_ms:  # Convert to ms
            matched_indices.append((i, j))
    
    # Align data
    aligned_a = eeg_a[[i for i, _ in matched_indices]]
    aligned_b = eeg_b[[j for _, j in matched_indices]]
    
    return aligned_a, aligned_b


# Function 39: Pupillometry Dynamics
def analyze_pupillometry(pupil_diameter, fs=1000):
    """
    Analyze pupil diameter fluctuations
    """
    from scipy import signal
    import numpy as np
    
    # Remove blinks (simple threshold)
    pupil_clean = pupil_diameter.copy()
    pupil_clean[pupil_clean < np.percentile(pupil_clean, 1)] = np.nan
    pupil_clean[pupil_clean > np.percentile(pupil_clean, 99)] = np.nan
    
    # Interpolate missing values
    nans = np.isnan(pupil_clean)
    pupil_clean[nans] = np.interp(np.flatnonzero(nans), 
                                   np.flatnonzero(~nans), 
                                   pupil_clean[~nans])
    
    # Compute power spectrum
    f, psd = signal.welch(pupil_clean, fs, nperseg=fs*10)
    
    # Extract features
    features = {
        'mean': np.mean(pupil_clean),
        'std': np.std(pupil_clean),
        'power_low': np.trapz(psd[(f >= 0.01) & (f <= 0.05)]),
        'power_high': np.trapz(psd[(f >= 0.1) & (f <= 0.5)]),
        'peak_freq': f[np.argmax(psd)]
    }
    
    return features


# Function 40: Heart Rate Variability (HRV) Analysis
def analyze_hrv_comprehensive(rr_intervals, fs=1000):
    """
    Comprehensive HRV analysis including time and frequency domains
    """
    import numpy as np
    from scipy import signal
    
    rr = np.array(rr_intervals)
    
    # Time domain
    mean_rr = np.mean(rr)
    sdnn = np.std(rr)
    rmssd = np.sqrt(np.mean(np.diff(rr)**2))
    
    # Frequency domain (requires interpolation to regular sampling)
    t = np.cumsum(rr) / 1000  # convert to seconds
    t_interp = np.arange(0, t[-1], 0.25)  # 4 Hz resampling
    rr_interp = np.interp(t_interp, t, rr)
    
    f, psd = signal.welch(rr_interp, fs=4, nperseg=256)
    
    # Extract bands
    vlf = np.trapz(psd[(f >= 0.0033) & (f <= 0.04)])
    lf = np.trapz(psd[(f >= 0.04) & (f <= 0.15)])
    hf = np.trapz(psd[(f >= 0.15) & (f <= 0.4)])
    
    return {
        'mean_rr': mean_rr,
        'sdnn': sdnn,
        'rmssd': rmssd,
        'vlf': vlf,
        'lf': lf,
        'hf': hf,
        'lf_hf_ratio': lf / hf if hf > 0 else np.inf
    }


# Function 41: Standardized Psi Control Protocol
def run_bem_protocol(n_trials=100, feedback_delay=1000):
    """
    Implements Daryl Bem's precognition protocol with pre-registration
    """
    import numpy as np
    import pandas as pd
    
    # Pre-registered parameters
    results = []
    
    for trial in range(n_trials):
        # Randomly select which of two images will be shown
        actual_image = np.random.choice(['erotic', 'neutral'])
        
        # Participant "precognitively" chooses before image is selected
        # In actual experiment, this is after but participants don't know
        choice = np.random.choice(['erotic', 'neutral'])  # Simulated
        
        # Determine accuracy
        correct = choice == actual_image
        
        results.append({
            'trial': trial,
            'choice': choice,
            'actual': actual_image,
            'correct': correct
        })
    
    df = pd.DataFrame(results)
    
    # Analysis
    accuracy = df['correct'].mean()
    from scipy.stats import binom_test
    p_value = binom_test(df['correct'].sum(), n_trials, 0.5)
    
    return {'accuracy': accuracy, 'p_value': p_value, 'data': df}


# Function 42: Dopamine Blocking Protocol
def dopamine_blocking_analysis(accuracy_drug, accuracy_placebo):
    """
    Test if dopamine blocking reduces "psychic" accuracy
    """
    from scipy.stats import ttest_rel
    
    t_stat, p_value = ttest_rel(accuracy_drug, accuracy_placebo)
    d = compute_cohens_d(accuracy_drug, accuracy_placebo, paired=True)[0]
    
    return {'t': t_stat, 'p': p_value, 'd': d}


# Function 43: Dynamic Connectivity Analysis
def sliding_window_connectivity(eeg_data, window_size=30, step=5, fs=256):
    """
    Sliding-window correlation to map B axis in real-time
    """
    import numpy as np
    
    window_samples = int(window_size * fs)
    step_samples = int(step * fs)
    
    n_windows = (len(eeg_data) - window_samples) // step_samples + 1
    n_channels = eeg_data.shape[1]
    
    connectivity = np.zeros((n_windows, n_channels, n_channels))
    
    for w in range(n_windows):
        start = w * step_samples
        end = start + window_samples
        window_data = eeg_data[start:end, :]
        
        # Correlation matrix
        corr_mat = np.corrcoef(window_data.T)
        connectivity[w] = corr_mat
    
    return connectivity


# Function 44: TMS Boundary Perturbation
def tms_boundary_analysis(pre_tms_B, post_tms_B, sham_B=None):
    """
    Analyze effects of TMS to rTPJ on B index
    """
    from scipy.stats import ttest_rel
    
    # Active TMS effect
    t_stat, p_value = ttest_rel(post_tms_B, pre_tms_B)
    d = compute_cohens_d(post_tms_B, pre_tms_B, paired=True)[0]
    
    # Compare to sham if available
    if sham_B is not None:
        t_sham, p_sham = ttest_rel(sham_B, pre_tms_B)
        d_sham = compute_cohens_d(sham_B, pre_tms_B, paired=True)[0]
        
        # Test if active > sham
        t_compare, p_compare = ttest_rel(post_tms_B - pre_tms_B, 
                                          sham_B - pre_tms_B)
    else:
        t_compare = p_compare = None
    
    return {'t': t_stat, 'p': p_value, 'd': d,
            't_compare': t_compare, 'p_compare': p_compare}


# Function 45: Microbiome-Precision Correlation
def microbiome_precision_correlation(microbiome_data, precision_scores):
    """
    Correlate bacterial abundance with precision scores
    """
    import numpy as np
    from scipy.stats import pearsonr
    from sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression
    
    n_bacteria = microbiome_data.shape[1]
    correlations = []
    
    for i in range(n_bacteria):
        r, p = pearsonr(microbiome_data[:, i], precision_scores)
        correlations.append({'bacteria_idx': i, 'r': r, 'p': p})
    
    # Multiple regression for diversity indices
    diversity = np.sum(microbiome_data > 0, axis=1)  # species richness
    model = LinearRegression()
    model.fit(diversity.reshape(-1, 1), precision_scores)
    
    return {'correlations': correlations,
            'diversity_r': model.score(diversity.reshape(-1, 1), precision_scores),
            'diversity_coef': model.coef_[0]}
